| [![Image 2](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Albert_Einstein_signature_1934.svg/250px-Albert_Einstein_signature_1934.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Albert_Einstein_signature_1934.svg) |

**Albert Einstein**[[a]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-6) (14 March 1879– 18 April 1955) was a German-born [theoretical physicist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theoretical_physicist "Theoretical physicist") who is best known for developing the [theory of relativity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theory_of_relativity "Theory of relativity"). Einstein also made important contributions to [quantum theory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_quantum_theory "Old quantum theory").[[1]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-frs-1)[[5]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-YangHamilton2010-7) His [mass–energy equivalence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mass%E2%80%93energy_equivalence "Mass–energy equivalence") formula [_E_ = _mc_ 2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mass%E2%80%93energy_equivalence#Mass%E2%80%93velocity_relationship "Mass–energy equivalence"), which arises from [special relativity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special_relativity "Special relativity"), has been called "the world's most famous equation".[[6]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-LnLVo-8) He received the 1921 [Nobel Prize in Physics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physics "Nobel Prize in Physics") for his services to theoretical physics, and especially for his discovery of the law of the [photoelectric effect](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Photoelectric_effect "Photoelectric effect").[[7]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Nobel_Prize-9)

Born in the [German Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_Empire "German Empire"), Einstein moved to Switzerland in 1895, forsaking his [German citizenship](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_citizenship "German citizenship") (as a subject of the [Kingdom of Württemberg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_W%C3%BCrttemberg "Kingdom of Württemberg"))[[note 1]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-GEcitizen-4) the following year. In 1897, at the age of seventeen, he enrolled in the mathematics and physics teaching diploma program at the Swiss [federal polytechnic school](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ETH_Zurich "ETH Zurich") in [Zurich](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zurich "Zurich"), graduating in 1900. He acquired [Swiss citizenship](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Swiss_citizenship "Swiss citizenship") a year later, which he kept for the rest of his life, and afterwards secured a permanent position at the [Swiss Patent Office](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Swiss_Patent_Office "Swiss Patent Office") in [Bern](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bern "Bern"). In 1905, he submitted a successful PhD dissertation to the [University of Zurich](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Zurich "University of Zurich"). In 1914, he moved to Berlin to join the [Prussian Academy of Sciences](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prussian_Academy_of_Sciences "Prussian Academy of Sciences") and the [Humboldt University of Berlin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humboldt_University_of_Berlin "Humboldt University of Berlin"), becoming director of the [Kaiser Wilhelm Institute for Physics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kaiser_Wilhelm_Institute_for_Physics "Kaiser Wilhelm Institute for Physics") in 1917; he also became a German citizen again, this time as a subject of the [Kingdom of Prussia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia "Kingdom of Prussia").[[note 1]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-GEcitizen-4) In 1933, while Einstein was visiting the United States, [Adolf Hitler came to power](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adolf_Hitler%27s_rise_to_power "Adolf Hitler's rise to power") in Germany. Horrified by the [Nazi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_Germany "Nazi Germany") persecution of his fellow Jews,[[8]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-zE9Bz-10) he decided to remain in the US, and was granted [American citizenship](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_citizen "American citizen") in 1940.[[9]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-BoyerDubofsky2001-11) On the eve of [World War II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_II "World War II"), he endorsed [a letter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Einstein%E2%80%93Szilard_letter "Einstein–Szilard letter") to President [Franklin D. Roosevelt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt "Franklin D. Roosevelt") alerting him to the potential [German nuclear weapons program](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_nuclear_weapons_program "German nuclear weapons program") and recommending that the US begin [similar research](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manhattan_Project "Manhattan Project").

In 1905, sometimes described as his _[annus mirabilis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Annus\_mirabilis "Annus mirabilis")_ (miracle year), he published [four groundbreaking papers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Annus_mirabilis_papers "Annus mirabilis papers").[[10]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGalison2000377-12) In them, he outlined a theory of the photoelectric effect, explained [Brownian motion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brownian_motion "Brownian motion"), introduced his special theory of relativity, and demonstrated that if the special theory is correct, mass and energy are equivalent to each other. In 1915, he proposed a [general theory of relativity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_theory_of_relativity "General theory of relativity") that extended his system of mechanics to incorporate [gravitation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gravitation "Gravitation"). A cosmological paper that he published the following year laid out the implications of general relativity for the modeling of the structure and evolution of the [universe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universe "Universe") as a whole.[[11]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Nobel-13)[[12]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-NYT-20151124-14) In 1917, Einstein wrote a paper which introduced the concepts of [spontaneous emission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spontaneous_emission "Spontaneous emission") and [stimulated emission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stimulated_emission "Stimulated emission"), the latter of which is the core mechanism behind the [laser](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Laser "Laser") and [maser](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maser "Maser"), and which contained a trove of information that would be beneficial to developments in physics later on, such as [quantum electrodynamics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_electrodynamics "Quantum electrodynamics") and [quantum optics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_optics "Quantum optics").[[13]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-15)

In the middle part of his career, Einstein made important contributions to [statistical mechanics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistical_mechanics "Statistical mechanics") and quantum theory. Especially notable was his work on the quantum physics of [radiation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radiation "Radiation"), in which light consists of particles, subsequently called [photons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Photon "Photon"). With physicist [Satyendra Nath Bose](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Satyendra_Nath_Bose "Satyendra Nath Bose"), he laid the groundwork for [Bose–Einstein statistics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bose%E2%80%93Einstein_statistics "Bose–Einstein statistics"). For much of the last phase of his academic life, Einstein worked on two endeavors that ultimately proved unsuccessful. First, he advocated against quantum theory's introduction of fundamental randomness into science's picture of the world, objecting that God does not play dice.[[14]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-16) Second, he attempted to devise a [unified field theory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unified_field_theory "Unified field theory") by generalizing his geometric theory of gravitation to include [electromagnetism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electromagnetism "Electromagnetism"). As a result, he became increasingly isolated from mainstream [modern physics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modern_physics "Modern physics").

Life and career
---------------

### Childhood, youth and education

[![Image 3: A young boy with short hair and a round face, wearing a white collar and large bow, with vest, coat, skirt, and high boots. He is leaning against an ornate chair.](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Albert_Einstein_at_the_age_of_three_%281882%29.jpg/250px-Albert_Einstein_at_the_age_of_three_%281882%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Albert_Einstein_at_the_age_of_three_(1882).jpg)

Einstein in 1882, age 3

Albert Einstein was born in [Ulm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ulm "Ulm"),[[15]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Bio-17) in the Kingdom of Württemberg in the German Empire, on 14 March 1879. His parents, secular [Ashkenazi Jews](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ashkenazi_Jews "Ashkenazi Jews"), were [Hermann Einstein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hermann_Einstein "Hermann Einstein"), a salesman and engineer, and [Pauline Koch](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pauline_Koch "Pauline Koch"). In 1880, the family moved to [Munich](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Munich "Munich")'s borough of [Ludwigsvorstadt-Isarvorstadt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ludwigsvorstadt-Isarvorstadt "Ludwigsvorstadt-Isarvorstadt"), where Einstein's father and his uncle Jakob founded Elektrotechnische Fabrik J. Einstein & Cie, a company that manufactured electrical equipment based on [direct current](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direct_current "Direct current").[[15]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Bio-17) He often related a formative event from his youth, when he was sick in bed and his father brought him a [compass](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magnetic_compass "Magnetic compass"). This sparked his lifelong fascination with [electromagnetism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electromagnetism "Electromagnetism"). He realized that "Something deeply hidden had to be behind things."[[16]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson200713-18)

Albert attended St. Peter's [Catholic elementary school](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catholic_school "Catholic school") in Munich from the age of five. When he was eight, he was transferred to the [Luitpold Gymnasium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luitpold_Gymnasium "Luitpold Gymnasium"), where he received advanced primary and then secondary school education.[[17]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStachel2002[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidOAsQ_hFjhrACpgPA59_59%E2%80%9361]-19)

[![Image 4](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Hermann_einstein.jpg/250px-Hermann_einstein.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Hermann_einstein.jpg)

[![Image 5](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Pauline_Koch_edit.jpg/250px-Pauline_Koch_edit.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Pauline_Koch_edit.jpg)

In 1894, Hermann and Jakob's company tendered for a contract to install electric lighting in Munich, but without success—they lacked the capital that would have been required to update their technology from direct current to the more efficient, [alternating current](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alternating_current "Alternating current") alternative.[[18]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-EQyag-20) The failure of their bid forced them to sell their Munich factory and search for new opportunities elsewhere. The Einstein family moved to Italy, first to [Milan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Milan "Milan") and a few months later to [Pavia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pavia "Pavia"), where they settled in [Palazzo Cornazzani](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palazzo_Cornazzani "Palazzo Cornazzani").[[19]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-21) Einstein, then fifteen, stayed behind in Munich in order to finish his schooling. His father wanted him to study [electrical engineering](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electrical_engineering "Electrical engineering"), but he was a fractious pupil who found the Gymnasium's regimen and teaching methods far from congenial. He later wrote that the school's policy of strict [rote learning](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rote_learning "Rote learning") was harmful to creativity. At the end of December 1894, a letter from a doctor persuaded the Luitpold's authorities to release him from its care, and he joined his family in Pavia.[[20]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEF%C3%B6lsing199730%E2%80%9331-22) While in Italy as a teenager, he wrote an essay entitled "On the Investigation of the State of the [Ether](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aether_(classical_element) "Aether (classical element)") in a Magnetic Field".[[21]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Stachel2008-23)[[22]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-1RgTv-24)

Einstein excelled at physics and mathematics from an early age, and soon acquired the mathematical expertise normally only found in a child several years his senior. He began teaching himself [algebra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algebra "Algebra"), [calculus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Calculus "Calculus") and [Euclidean geometry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euclidean_geometry "Euclidean geometry") when he was twelve; he made such rapid progress that he discovered an original proof of the [Pythagorean theorem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pythagorean_theorem "Pythagorean theorem") before his thirteenth birthday.[[23]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FVfDU-25)[[24]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-26) A family tutor, [Max Talmud](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Max_Talmud "Max Talmud"), said that only a short time after he had given the twelve year old Einstein a geometry textbook, the boy had worked through the whole book. He thereupon devoted himself to higher mathematics... Soon the flight of his mathematical genius was so high I could not follow.[[25]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson200717-27) Einstein recorded that he had "mastered [integral](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Integral "Integral") and [differential calculus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Differential_calculus "Differential calculus")" while still just fourteen.[[26]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson200716-28) His love of algebra and geometry was so great that at twelve, he was already confident that nature could be understood as a "mathematical structure".[[27]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson200717%E2%80%9318-29)

[![Image 6: Studio photo of a boy seated in a relaxed posture and wearing a suit, posed in front of a backdrop of scenery.](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Albert_Einstein_as_a_child.jpg/250px-Albert_Einstein_as_a_child.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Albert_Einstein_as_a_child.jpg)

Einstein in 1893, age 14

At thirteen, when his range of enthusiasms had broadened to include music and philosophy,[[28]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalapriceLipscombe20058-30) Talmud introduced Einstein to [Kant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kant "Kant")'s _[Critique of Pure Reason](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Critique\_of\_Pure\_Reason "Critique of Pure Reason")_. Kant became his favorite philosopher; according to Talmud, At the time he was still a child, only thirteen years old, yet Kant's works, incomprehensible to ordinary mortals, seemed to be clear to him.[[25]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson200717-27)

In 1895, at the age of sixteen, Einstein sat the entrance examination for the [federal polytechnic school](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ETH_Zurich "ETH Zurich") (later the Eidgenössische Technische Hochschule, ETH) in Zurich, Switzerland. He failed to reach the required standard in the general part of the test,[[29]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Stachel2008a-31) but performed with distinction in physics and mathematics.[[30]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEF%C3%B6lsing199736%E2%80%9337-32) On the advice of the polytechnic's principal, he completed his secondary education at the [Argovian cantonal school](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Cantonal_School_Aarau "Old Cantonal School Aarau") (a [_gymnasium_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gymnasium_(school) "Gymnasium (school)")) in [Aarau](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aarau "Aarau"), Switzerland, graduating in 1896.[[31]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-b250-33) While lodging in Aarau with the family of [Jost Winteler](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jost_Winteler "Jost Winteler"), he fell in love with Winteler's daughter, Marie. (His sister, [Maja](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maja_Einstein "Maja Einstein"), later married Winteler's son Paul.[[32]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHighfieldCarter199321,_31,_56%E2%80%9357-34))

[![Image 7: Einstein's matriculation certificate at the age of 17. The heading translates as "The Education Committee of the Canton of Aargau". His scores were German 5, French 3, Italian 5, History 6, Geography 4, Algebra 6, Geometry 6, Descriptive Geometry 6, Physics 6, Chemistry 5, Natural History 5, Art Drawing 4, Technical Drawing 4. 6 = very good, 5 = good, 4 = sufficient, 3 = insufficient, 2 = poor, 1 = very poor.](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Albert_Einstein%27s_exam_of_maturity_grades_%28color2%29.jpg/250px-Albert_Einstein%27s_exam_of_maturity_grades_%28color2%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Albert_Einstein%27s_exam_of_maturity_grades_(color2).jpg)

Einstein's _[Matura](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Matura "Matura")_ certificate from canton [Aargau](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aargau "Aargau"), 1896[[note 2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-MaturaScore-35)

In January 1896, with his father's approval, Einstein renounced his [citizenship of the German Kingdom of Württemberg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_citizenship "German citizenship") in order to avoid [conscription into military service](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conscription_in_Germany "Conscription in Germany").[[33]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEF%C3%B6lsing199740-36) The _[Matura](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Matura "Matura")_ (graduation for the successful completion of higher secondary schooling), awarded to him in September 1896, acknowledged him to have performed well across most of the curriculum, allotting him a [top grade of 6](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grading_systems_by_country#Switzerland "Grading systems by country") for history, physics, algebra, geometry, and descriptive geometry.[[34]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Stachel2008b-37) At seventeen, he enrolled in the four-year mathematics and physics teaching diploma program at the federal polytechnic school. Marie Winteler, a year older than him, took up a teaching post in [Olsberg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Olsberg,_Aargau "Olsberg, Aargau"), Switzerland.[[32]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHighfieldCarter199321,_31,_56%E2%80%9357-34)

The five other polytechnic school freshmen following the same course as Einstein included just one woman, a twenty year old [Serbian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Serbs "Serbs"), [Mileva Marić](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mileva_Mari%C4%87 "Mileva Marić"). Over the next few years, the pair spent many hours discussing their shared interests and learning about topics in physics that the polytechnic school's lectures did not cover. In his letters to Marić, Einstein confessed that exploring science with her by his side was much more enjoyable than reading a textbook in solitude. Eventually the two students became not only friends but also lovers.[[35]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-mileva-38)

Historians of physics are divided on the question of the extent to which Marić contributed to the insights of Einstein's _annus mirabilis_ publications. There is at least some evidence that he was influenced by her scientific ideas,[[35]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-mileva-38)[[36]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-7HA7H-39)[[37]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-1zJdH-40) but there are scholars who doubt whether her impact on his thought was of any great significance at all.[[38]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPais19941%E2%80%9329-41)[[39]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-xKrMG-42)[[40]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStachel2002[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidOAsQ_hFjhrACpgPA49_49%E2%80%9356]-43)[[41]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-dUxMl-44)

### Marriages, relationships and children

[![Image 8](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Albert_Einstein_and_his_wife_Mileva_Maric.jpg/250px-Albert_Einstein_and_his_wife_Mileva_Maric.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Albert_Einstein_and_his_wife_Mileva_Maric.jpg)

Albert Einstein and [Mileva Marić](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mileva_Mari%C4%87 "Mileva Marić") Einstein, 1912

Correspondence between Einstein and Marić, discovered and published in 1987, revealed that in early 1902, while Marić was visiting her parents in [Novi Sad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Novi_Sad "Novi Sad"), she gave birth to a daughter, [Lieserl](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lieserl_Einstein "Lieserl Einstein"). When Marić returned to Switzerland it was without the child, whose fate is uncertain. A letter of Einstein's that he wrote in September 1903 suggests that the girl was either given up for adoption or died of [scarlet fever](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scarlet_fever "Scarlet fever") in infancy.[[42]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-HBMes-45)[[43]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalapriceLipscombe200522%E2%80%9323-46)

Einstein and Marić married in January 1903. In May 1904, their son [Hans Albert](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hans_Albert_Einstein "Hans Albert Einstein") was born in [Bern](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bern "Bern"), Switzerland. Their son [Eduard](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Einstein_family#Eduard_%22Tete%22_Einstein_(Albert's_second_son) "Einstein family") was born in Zurich in July 1910. In letters that Einstein wrote to Marie Winteler in the months before Eduard's arrival, he described his love for his wife as "misguided" and mourned the "missed life" that he imagined he would have enjoyed if he had married Winteler instead: "I think of you in heartfelt love every spare minute and am so unhappy as only a man can be."[[44]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-MlQLY-47)

[![Image 9: Einstein, looking relaxed and holding a pipe, stands next to a smiling, well-dressed Elsa who is wearing a fancy hat and fur wrap. She is looking at him.](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Einstein_Albert_Elsa_LOC_32096u.jpg/250px-Einstein_Albert_Elsa_LOC_32096u.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Einstein_Albert_Elsa_LOC_32096u.jpg)

Albert and [Elsa Einstein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elsa_Einstein "Elsa Einstein") arriving in New York, 1921

In 1912, Einstein entered into a relationship with [Elsa Löwenthal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elsa_L%C3%B6wenthal "Elsa Löwenthal"), who was both his first cousin on his mother's side and his second cousin on his father's.[[45]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalapriceLipscombe2005[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid5eWh2O_3OAQCpgPA50_50]-48)[[46]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-dh-49)[[47]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStachel1966-50) When Marić learned of his infidelity soon after moving to Berlin with him in April 1914, she returned to Zurich, taking Hans Albert and Eduard with her.[[35]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-mileva-38) Einstein and Marić were granted a divorce on 14 February 1919 on the grounds of having lived apart for five years.[[48]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-51)[[49]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStachel2002[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidOAsQ_hFjhrACpgPA50_50]-52) As part of the divorce settlement, Einstein agreed that if he were to win a Nobel Prize, he would give the money that he received to Marić; he won the prize two years later.[[50]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-53)

Einstein married Löwenthal in 1919.[[51]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007xix-54)[[52]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalapriceKennefickSchulmann201562-55) In 1923, he began a relationship with a secretary named Betty Neumann, the niece of his close friend Hans Mühsam.[[53]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-56)[[54]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-57)[[55]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-58)[[56]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-59) Löwenthal nevertheless remained loyal to him, accompanying him when he emigrated to the United States in 1933. In 1935, she was diagnosed with heart and kidney problems. She died in December 1936.[[57]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHighfieldCarter1993216-60)

[![Image 10](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Albert_Einstein_and_Elsa_Einstein_arriving_by_ship%2C_San_Diego%2C_1930_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Albert_Einstein_and_Elsa_Einstein_arriving_by_ship%2C_San_Diego%2C_1930_%28cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Albert_Einstein_and_Elsa_Einstein_arriving_by_ship,_San_Diego,_1930_(cropped).jpg)

Albert and Elsa Einstein, 1930

A volume of Einstein's letters released by [Hebrew University of Jerusalem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hebrew_University_of_Jerusalem "Hebrew University of Jerusalem") in 2006[[58]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-61) added some other women with whom he was romantically involved. They included Margarete Lebach (a married Austrian),[[59]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-62) Estella Katzenellenbogen (the rich owner of a florist business), Toni Mendel (a wealthy Jewish widow) and Ethel Michanowski (a Berlin socialite), with whom he spent time and from whom he accepted gifts while married to Löwenthal.[[60]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-63)[[61]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-64) After being widowed, Einstein was briefly in a relationship with Margarita Konenkova, thought by some to be a Russian spy; her husband, the Russian sculptor [Sergei Konenkov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sergei_Konenkov "Sergei Konenkov"), created the bronze bust of Einstein at the [Institute for Advanced Study](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Institute_for_Advanced_Study "Institute for Advanced Study") at Princeton.[[62]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-65)[[63]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-66)

Following an episode of acute mental illness at about the age of twenty, Einstein's son Eduard was diagnosed with [schizophrenia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Schizophrenia "Schizophrenia").[[64]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Robinson2015a-67) He spent the remainder of his life either in the care of his mother or in temporary confinement in an asylum. After her death, he was committed permanently to [Burghölzli](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Burgh%C3%B6lzli "Burghölzli"), the Psychiatric University Hospital in Zurich.[[65]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeffe2007[httpsarchiveorgdetailseinsteinbiograph00neffpage203_203]-68)

### Assistant at the Swiss Patent Office (1902–1909)

[![Image 11: Head and shoulders shot of a young, mustached man with dark, curly hair wearing a plaid suit and vest, striped shirt, and a dark tie.](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Einstein_patentoffice_full_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Einstein_patentoffice_full_%28cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Einstein_patentoffice_full_(cropped).jpg)

Einstein at the [Swiss patent office](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Swiss_patent_office "Swiss patent office"), 1904

Einstein graduated from the federal polytechnic school in 1900, duly certified as competent to teach mathematics and physics.[[66]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-69) His successful acquisition of Swiss citizenship in February 1901[[67]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEF%C3%B6lsing199782-70) was not followed by the usual sequel of [conscription](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conscription_in_Switzerland "Conscription in Switzerland"); the Swiss authorities deemed him medically unfit for military service. He found that Swiss schools too appeared to have no use for him, failing to offer him a teaching position despite the almost two years that he spent applying for one. Eventually it was with the help of [Marcel Grossmann](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marcel_Grossmann "Marcel Grossmann")'s father that he secured a post in [Bern](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bern "Bern") at the [Swiss Patent Office](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Swiss_Patent_Office "Swiss Patent Office"),[[68]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-ODY5p-71)[[69]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson200763-72) as an [assistant examiner – level III](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Patent_examiner "Patent examiner").[[70]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-MeZPN-73)[[71]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-IGEFAQ-74)

[Patent applications](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Patent_application "Patent application") that landed on Einstein's desk for his evaluation included ideas for a gravel sorter and an electric typewriter.[[71]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-IGEFAQ-74) His employers were pleased enough with his work to make his position permanent in 1903, although they did not think that he should be promoted until he had "fully mastered machine technology".[[72]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGalison2000370-75) It is conceivable that his labors at the patent office had a bearing on his development of his special theory of relativity. He arrived at his revolutionary ideas about space, time and light through thought experiments about the transmission of signals and the synchronization of clocks, matters which also figured in some of the inventions submitted to him for assessment.[[10]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGalison2000377-12)

In 1902, Einstein and some friends whom he had met in Bern formed a group that held regular meetings to discuss science and philosophy. Their choice of a name for their club, the [Olympia Academy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Olympia_Academy "Olympia Academy"), was an ironic comment upon its far from Olympian status. Sometimes they were joined by Marić, who limited her participation in their proceedings to careful listening.[[73]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHighfieldCarter199396%E2%80%9398-76) The thinkers whose works they reflected upon included [Henri Poincaré](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henri_Poincar%C3%A9 "Henri Poincaré"), [Ernst Mach](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ernst_Mach "Ernst Mach") and [David Hume](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Hume "David Hume"), all of whom significantly influenced Einstein's own subsequent ideas and beliefs.[[74]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson200779%E2%80%9384-77)

### First scientific papers (1900–1905)

[![Image 12: Cover image of the PhD dissertation of Albert Einstein](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Einstein_thesis.png/250px-Einstein_thesis.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Einstein_thesis.png)

Einstein's 1905 dissertation, _Eine neue Be­stimm­ung der Mol­e­kül­di­men­si­onen_ ("A new deter­mi­na­tion of mo­lec­u­lar di­men­sions")

Einstein's first paper, ["Folgerungen aus den Capillaritätserscheinungen"](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_scientific_publications_by_Albert_Einstein#Journal_articles "List of scientific publications by Albert Einstein") ("Conclusions drawn from the phenomena of capillarity"), in which he proposed a model of intermolecular attraction that he afterwards disavowed as worthless, was published in the journal _[Annalen der Physik](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Annalen\_der\_Physik "Annalen der Physik")_ in 1901.[[75]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Einstein_1901-78)[[76]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-79) His 24-page doctoral dissertation also addressed a topic in molecular physics. Titled "Eine neue Bestimmung der Moleküldimensionen" ("A New Determination of Molecular Dimensions") and dedicated "Meinem Freunde Herr Dr. Marcel Grossmann gewidmet" (to his friend Marcel Grossman), it was completed on 30 April 1905[[77]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-1905b-80) and approved by Professor [Alfred Kleiner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alfred_Kleiner "Alfred Kleiner") of the University of Zurich three months later. (Einstein was formally awarded his PhD on 15 January 1906.)[[77]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-1905b-80)[[78]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-81)[[79]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-82) Four other pieces of work that Einstein completed in 1905—[his famous papers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Annus_mirabilis_papers "Annus mirabilis papers") on the [photoelectric effect](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Photoelectric_effect "Photoelectric effect"), [Brownian motion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brownian_motion "Brownian motion"), his [special theory of relativity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special_theory_of_relativity "Special theory of relativity") and the [equivalence of mass and energy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Equivalence_of_mass_and_energy "Equivalence of mass and energy")—have led to the year being celebrated as an _annus mirabilis_ for physics akin to the miracle year of 1666 when [Isaac Newton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isaac_Newton "Isaac Newton") experienced his greatest epiphanies. The publications deeply impressed Einstein's contemporaries.[[80]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-83)

### Academic career in Europe (1908–1933)

Einstein's sabbatical as a civil servant approached its end in 1908, when he secured a junior teaching position at the [University of Bern](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Bern "University of Bern"). In 1909, a lecture on relativistic [electrodynamics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electrodynamics "Electrodynamics") that he gave at the University of Zurich, much admired by [Alfred Kleiner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alfred_Kleiner "Alfred Kleiner"), led to Zurich's luring him away from Bern with a newly created associate professorship.[[81]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-bG2yp-84) Promotion to a full professorship followed in April 1911, when he took up a chair at the German [Charles-Ferdinand University](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles-Ferdinand_University "Charles-Ferdinand University") in [Prague](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prague "Prague"),[[82]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordin2020[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidoJ27DwAAQBAJpgPA45_45]-85) a move which required him to become an [Austrian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cisleithania "Cisleithania") citizen of the [Austro-Hungarian Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Austro-Hungarian_Empire "Austro-Hungarian Empire"), which was not completed.[[83]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordin2020[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidoJ27DwAAQBAJpgPA14_20]-86) His time in Prague saw him producing eleven research papers.[[84]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-87)

[![Image 13](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/ETH-BIB-Einstein%2C_Albert_und_Kollegen_am_Physik-Labor_ETH-Portrait-Portr_10750.tif/lossy-page1-280px-ETH-BIB-Einstein%2C_Albert_und_Kollegen_am_Physik-Labor_ETH-Portrait-Portr_10750.tif.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:ETH-BIB-Einstein,_Albert_und_Kollegen_am_Physik-Labor_ETH-Portrait-Portr_10750.tif)

Einstein with colleagues at the [ETH](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ETH "ETH") in [Zurich](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zurich "Zurich"), 1913

From 30 October to 3 November 1911, Einstein attended the first [Solvay Conference on Physics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solvay_Conference#First_conference "Solvay Conference").[[85]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-88)

In July 1912, he returned to his _alma mater_, the [ETH Zurich](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ETH_Zurich "ETH Zurich"), to take up a chair in theoretical physics. His teaching activities there centered on [thermodynamics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thermodynamics "Thermodynamics") and analytical mechanics, and his research interests included the molecular theory of heat, [continuum mechanics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Continuum_mechanics "Continuum mechanics") and the development of a relativistic theory of gravitation. In his work on the latter topic, he was assisted by his friend Marcel Grossmann, whose knowledge of the kind of mathematics required was greater than his own.[[86]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-hXQin-89)

In the spring of 1913, two German visitors, [Max Planck](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Max_Planck "Max Planck") and [Walther Nernst](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Walther_Nernst "Walther Nernst"), called upon Einstein in Zurich in the hope of persuading him to relocate to Berlin.[[87]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStachel2002534-90) They offered him membership of the [Prussian Academy of Sciences](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prussian_Academy_of_Sciences "Prussian Academy of Sciences"), the directorship of the planned [Kaiser Wilhelm Institute for Physics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kaiser_Wilhelm_Institute_for_Physics "Kaiser Wilhelm Institute for Physics") and a chair at the [Humboldt University of Berlin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humboldt_University_of_Berlin "Humboldt University of Berlin") that would allow him to pursue his research supported by a professorial salary but with no teaching duties to burden him.[[46]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-dh-49) Their invitation was all the more appealing to him because Berlin happened to be the home of his latest girlfriend, Elsa Löwenthal.[[87]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStachel2002534-90) He duly joined the Academy on 24 July 1913,[[88]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-jstor.org-91) and moved into an apartment in the Berlin district of [Dahlem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dahlem_(Berlin) "Dahlem (Berlin)") on 1 April 1914.[[46]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-dh-49) He was installed in his Humboldt University position shortly thereafter.[[88]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-jstor.org-91)

[![Image 14](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Berliner_Physiker_u_Chemiker_1920.jpg/330px-Berliner_Physiker_u_Chemiker_1920.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Berliner_Physiker_u_Chemiker_1920.jpg)

Einstein with other physicists and chemists in Berlin, 1920

The outbreak of the [First World War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_World_War "First World War") in July 1914 marked the beginning of Einstein's gradual estrangement from the nation of his birth. When the "[Manifesto of the Ninety-Three](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manifesto_of_the_Ninety-Three "Manifesto of the Ninety-Three")" was published in October 1914—a document signed by a host of prominent German thinkers that justified Germany's belligerence—Einstein was one of the few German intellectuals to distance himself from it and sign the alternative, eirenic "[Manifesto to the Europeans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manifesto_to_the_Europeans "Manifesto to the Europeans")" instead.[[89]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEScheideler2002333-92) However, this expression of his doubts about German policy did not prevent him from being elected to a two-year term as president of the [German Physical Society](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_Physical_Society "German Physical Society") in 1916.[[90]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalapriceLipscombe2005[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid5eWh2O_3OAQCpgPR19_%22Timeline%22,_p._xix]-93) When the Kaiser Wilhelm Institute for Physics opened its doors the following year—its foundation delayed because of the war—Einstein was appointed its first director, just as Planck and Nernst had promised.[[91]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-EXcH6-94)

Einstein was elected a Foreign Member of the [Royal Netherlands Academy of Arts and Sciences](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Royal_Netherlands_Academy_of_Arts_and_Sciences "Royal Netherlands Academy of Arts and Sciences") in 1920,[[92]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-3gcYy-95) and a [Foreign Member of the Royal Society in 1921](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Fellows_of_the_Royal_Society_elected_in_1921 "List of Fellows of the Royal Society elected in 1921"). In 1922, he was awarded the 1921 [Nobel Prize in Physics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physics "Nobel Prize in Physics") "for his services to Theoretical Physics, and especially for his discovery of the law of the photoelectric effect".[[7]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Nobel_Prize-9) At this point some physicists still regarded the general theory of relativity skeptically, and the Nobel citation displayed a degree of doubt even about the work on photoelectricity that it acknowledged: it did not assent to Einstein's notion of the particulate nature of light, which only won over the entire scientific community when [S. N. Bose](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/S._N._Bose "S. N. Bose") derived the [Planck spectrum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planck_spectrum "Planck spectrum") in 1924. That same year, Einstein was elected an International Honorary Member of the [American Academy of Arts and Sciences](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Academy_of_Arts_and_Sciences "American Academy of Arts and Sciences").[[93]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-96) Britain's closest equivalent of the Nobel award, the [Royal Society](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Royal_Society "Royal Society")'s [Copley Medal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Copley_Medal "Copley Medal"), was not hung around Einstein's neck until 1925.[[1]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-frs-1) He was elected an International Member of the [American Philosophical Society](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Philosophical_Society "American Philosophical Society") in 1930.[[94]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-97)

Einstein resigned from the Prussian Academy in March 1933. His accomplishments in Berlin had included the completion of the general theory of relativity, proving the [Einstein–de Haas effect](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Einstein%E2%80%93de_Haas_effect "Einstein–de Haas effect"), contributing to the quantum theory of radiation, and the development of [Bose–Einstein statistics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bose%E2%80%93Einstein_statistics "Bose–Einstein statistics").[[46]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-dh-49)

### Putting general relativity to the test (1919)

[![Image 15](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/19191125_A_New_Physics_Based_on_Einstein_-_The_New_York_Times.png/250px-19191125_A_New_Physics_Based_on_Einstein_-_The_New_York_Times.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:19191125_A_New_Physics_Based_on_Einstein_-_The_New_York_Times.png)

_[The New York Times](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_New\_York\_Times "The New York Times")_ reported confirmation of the bending of light by gravitation after observations (made in [Príncipe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pr%C3%ADncipe "Príncipe") and [Sobral](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sobral,_Cear%C3%A1 "Sobral, Ceará")) of the 29 May 1919 eclipse were presented to a joint meeting in London of the [Royal Society](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Royal_Society "Royal Society") and the [Royal Astronomical Society](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Royal_Astronomical_Society "Royal Astronomical Society") on 6 November 1919.[[95]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-NYTimes_19191125-98)

In 1907, Einstein reached a milestone on his long journey from his special theory of relativity to a new idea of gravitation with the formulation of his [equivalence principle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Equivalence_principle "Equivalence principle"), which asserts that an observer in a box falling freely in a gravitational field would be unable to find any evidence that the field exists. In 1911, he used the principle to estimate the amount by which a ray of light from a distant star would be [bent](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gravitational_lens "Gravitational lens") by the gravitational pull of the Sun as it passed close to the Sun's [photosphere](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Photosphere "Photosphere") (that is, the Sun's apparent surface). He reworked his calculation in 1913, having now found a way to model gravitation with the [Riemann curvature tensor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Riemann_curvature_tensor "Riemann curvature tensor") of a non-Euclidean four-dimensional [spacetime](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spacetime "Spacetime"). By the fall of 1915, his reimagining of the mathematics of gravitation in terms of Riemannian geometry was complete, and he applied his new theory not just to the behavior of the Sun as a gravitational lens but also to another astronomical phenomenon, the [precession of the perihelion of Mercury](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Precession_of_the_perihelion_of_Mercury "Precession of the perihelion of Mercury") (a slow drift in the point in Mercury's elliptical orbit at which it approaches the Sun most closely).[[46]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-dh-49)[[96]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-99) A [total eclipse of the Sun that took place on 29 May 1919](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_eclipse_of_May_29,_1919 "Solar eclipse of May 29, 1919") provided an opportunity to put his theory of gravitational lensing to the test, and observations performed by Sir [Arthur Eddington](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arthur_Eddington "Arthur Eddington") yielded results that were consistent with his calculations. Eddington's work was reported at length in newspapers around the world. On 7 November 1919, for example, the leading British newspaper, _[The Times](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Times "The Times")_, printed a banner headline that read: Revolution in Science– New Theory of the Universe– Newtonian Ideas Overthrown.[[97]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Eddington-100)

### Coming to terms with fame (1921–1923)

[![Image 16](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Albert_Einstein_%28Nobel%29.png/250px-Albert_Einstein_%28Nobel%29.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Albert_Einstein_(Nobel).png)

Einstein's official portrait after receiving the 1921 [Nobel Prize](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nobel_Prize "Nobel Prize") for Physics

With Eddington's eclipse observations widely reported not just in academic journals but by the popular press as well, Einstein became perhaps the world's first celebrity scientist, a genius who had shattered a paradigm that had been basic to physicists' understanding of the universe since the seventeenth century.[[98]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-101)

Einstein began his new life as an intellectual icon in America, where he arrived on 2 April 1921. He was welcomed to New York City by Mayor [John Francis Hylan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Francis_Hylan "John Francis Hylan"), and then spent three weeks giving lectures and attending receptions.[[99]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-102) He spoke several times at [Columbia University](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Columbia_University "Columbia University") and [Princeton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Princeton "Princeton"), and in Washington, he visited the [White House](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_House "White House") with representatives of the [National Academy of Sciences](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Academy_of_Sciences "National Academy of Sciences"). He returned to Europe via London, where he was the guest of the philosopher and statesman [Viscount Haldane](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Viscount_Haldane "Viscount Haldane"). He used his time in the British capital to meet several people prominent in British scientific, political or intellectual life, and to deliver a lecture at [King's College](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/King%27s_College_London "King's College London").[[100]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoffmann1972145%E2%80%93148-103)[[101]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEF%C3%B6lsing1997499%E2%80%93508-104) In July 1921, he published an essay, "My First Impression of the U.S.A.", in which he sought to sketch the American character, much as had [Alexis de Tocqueville](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexis_de_Tocqueville "Alexis de Tocqueville") in _[Democracy in America](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democracy\_in\_America "Democracy in America")_ (1835).[[102]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-7gwHd-105) He wrote of his transatlantic hosts in highly approving terms: What strikes a visitor is the joyous, positive attitude to life ... The American is friendly, self-confident, optimistic, and without envy.[[103]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHolton198420-106)

In 1922, Einstein's travels were to the old world rather than the new. He devoted six months to a tour of Asia that saw him speaking in Japan, Singapore and Sri Lanka (then known as [Ceylon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ceylon "Ceylon")). After his first public lecture in Tokyo, he met [Emperor Yoshihito](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emperor_Yoshihito "Emperor Yoshihito") and his wife at the [Imperial Palace](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tokyo_Imperial_Palace "Tokyo Imperial Palace"), with thousands of spectators thronging the streets in the hope of catching a glimpse of him. (In a letter to his sons, he wrote that Japanese people seemed to him to be generally modest, intelligent and considerate, and to have a true appreciation of art.[[104]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007307%E2%80%93308-107) But his picture of them in his diary was less flattering: [the] intellectual needs of this nation seem to be weaker than their artistic ones – natural disposition? His journal also contains views of China and India which were uncomplimentary. Of Chinese people, he wrote that even the children are spiritless and look obtuse... It would be a pity if these Chinese supplant all other races. For the likes of us the mere thought is unspeakably dreary.[[105]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-38YkY-108)[[106]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-109)) He was greeted with even greater enthusiasm on the last leg of his tour, in which he spent twelve days in [Mandatory Palestine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mandatory_Palestine "Mandatory Palestine"), newly entrusted to British rule by the [League of Nations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/League_of_Nations "League of Nations") in the aftermath of the First World War. [Sir Herbert Samuel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sir_Herbert_Samuel "Sir Herbert Samuel"), the British High Commissioner, welcomed him with a degree of ceremony normally only accorded to a visiting head of state, including a cannon salute. One reception held in his honor was stormed by people determined to hear him speak: he told them that he was happy that Jews were beginning to be recognized as a force in the world.[[104]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007307%E2%80%93308-107)

Einstein's decision to tour the eastern hemisphere in 1922 meant that he was unable to go to [Stockholm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stockholm "Stockholm") in the December of that year to participate in the Nobel prize ceremony. His place at the traditional Nobel banquet was taken by a German diplomat, who gave a speech praising him not only as a physicist but also as a campaigner for peace.[[107]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-oxak7-110) A two-week visit to Spain that he undertook in 1923 saw him collecting another award, a membership of the Spanish Academy of Sciences signified by a diploma handed to him by King [Alfonso XIII](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alfonso_XIII "Alfonso XIII"). (His Spanish trip also gave him a chance to meet a fellow Nobel laureate, the neuroanatomist [Santiago Ramón y Cajal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Santiago_Ram%C3%B3n_y_Cajal "Santiago Ramón y Cajal").)[[108]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-w74nv-111)

### Serving the League of Nations (1922–1932)

[![Image 17](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/League_of_Nations_Commission_067.tif/lossy-page1-250px-League_of_Nations_Commission_067.tif.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:League_of_Nations_Commission_067.tif)

Einstein at a session of the [International Committee on Intellectual Cooperation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Committee_on_Intellectual_Cooperation "International Committee on Intellectual Cooperation") ([League of Nations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/League_of_Nations "League of Nations")) of which he was a member from 1922 to 1932

From 1922 until 1932, with the exception of a few months in 1923 and 1924, Einstein was a member of the Geneva-based [International Committee on Intellectual Cooperation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Committee_on_Intellectual_Cooperation "International Committee on Intellectual Cooperation") of the [League of Nations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/League_of_Nations "League of Nations"), a group set up by the League to encourage scientists, artists, scholars, teachers and other people engaged in the life of the mind to work more closely with their counterparts in other countries.[[109]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Q5hgx-112)[[110]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-vNNnX-113) He was appointed as a German delegate rather than as a representative of Switzerland because of the machinations of two Catholic activists, [Oskar Halecki](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oskar_Halecki "Oskar Halecki") and [Giuseppe Motta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Giuseppe_Motta "Giuseppe Motta"). By persuading Secretary General [Eric Drummond](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eric_Drummond "Eric Drummond") to deny Einstein the place on the committee reserved for a Swiss thinker, they created an opening for [Gonzague de Reynold](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gonzague_de_Reynold "Gonzague de Reynold"), who used his League of Nations position as a platform from which to promote traditional Catholic doctrine.[[111]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-e9Xyh-114) Einstein's former physics professor [Hendrik Lorentz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hendrik_Lorentz "Hendrik Lorentz") and the Polish chemist [Marie Curie](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marie_Curie "Marie Curie") were also members of the committee.[[112]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-115)

### Touring South America (1925)

In March and April 1925, Einstein and his wife visited South America, where they spent about a week in Brazil, a week in Uruguay and a month in Argentina.[[113]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-116) Their tour was suggested by Jorge Duclout (1856–1927) and Mauricio Nirenstein (1877–1935)[[114]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-117) with the support of several Argentine scholars, including [Julio Rey Pastor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Julio_Rey_Pastor "Julio Rey Pastor"), [Jakob Laub](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jakob_Laub "Jakob Laub"), and [Leopoldo Lugones](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leopoldo_Lugones "Leopoldo Lugones"). and was financed primarily by the Council of the [University of Buenos Aires](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Buenos_Aires "University of Buenos Aires") and the _Asociación Hebraica Argentina_ (Argentine Hebraic Association) with a smaller contribution from the Argentine-Germanic Cultural Institution.[[115]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-118)

### Touring the US (1930–1931)

[![Image 18](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Albert_Einstein_writing_on_a_blackboard_in_Pasadena_%281931%29.jpg/250px-Albert_Einstein_writing_on_a_blackboard_in_Pasadena_%281931%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Albert_Einstein_writing_on_a_blackboard_in_Pasadena_(1931).jpg)

Einstein in [Pasadena, California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pasadena,_California "Pasadena, California"), 1931

In December 1930, Einstein began another significant sojourn in the United States, drawn back to the US by the offer of a two month research fellowship at the [California Institute of Technology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_Institute_of_Technology "California Institute of Technology"). Caltech supported him in his wish that he should not be exposed to quite as much attention from the media as he had experienced when visiting the US in 1921, and he therefore declined all the invitations to receive prizes or make speeches that his admirers poured down upon him. But he remained willing to allow his fans at least some of the time with him that they requested.[[116]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007368-119)

After arriving in New York City, Einstein was taken to various places and events, including [Chinatown](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chinatown,_Manhattan "Chinatown, Manhattan"), a lunch with the editors of _The New York Times_, and a performance of _[Carmen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carmen "Carmen")_ at the [Metropolitan Opera](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metropolitan_Opera "Metropolitan Opera"), where he was cheered by the audience on his arrival. During the days following, he was given the keys to the city by Mayor [Jimmy Walker](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jimmy_Walker "Jimmy Walker") and met [Nicholas Murray Butler](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nicholas_Murray_Butler "Nicholas Murray Butler"), the president of [Columbia University](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Columbia_University "Columbia University"), who described Einstein as "the ruling monarch of the mind".[[117]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007370-120)[Harry Emerson Fosdick](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Emerson_Fosdick "Harry Emerson Fosdick"), pastor at New York's [Riverside Church](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Riverside_Church "Riverside Church"), gave Einstein a tour of the church and showed him a full-size statue that the church made of Einstein, standing at the entrance.[[117]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007370-120) Also during his stay in New York, he joined a crowd of 15,000 people at [Madison Square Garden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden_(1925) "Madison Square Garden (1925)") during a [Hanukkah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hanukkah "Hanukkah") celebration.[[117]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007370-120)

[![Image 19](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Albert_Einstein_and_Charlie_Chaplin_City_Lights_premiere_1931.jpg/250px-Albert_Einstein_and_Charlie_Chaplin_City_Lights_premiere_1931.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Albert_Einstein_and_Charlie_Chaplin_City_Lights_premiere_1931.jpg)

Einstein with [Charlie Chaplin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charlie_Chaplin "Charlie Chaplin") at the [Hollywood](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hollywood,_Los_Angeles "Hollywood, Los Angeles") premiere of Chaplin's _[City Lights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/City\_Lights "City Lights")_, January 1931

Einstein next traveled to California, where he met [Caltech](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caltech "Caltech") president and Nobel laureate [Robert A. Millikan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_A._Millikan "Robert A. Millikan"). His friendship with Millikan was awkward, as Millikan had a penchant for patriotic militarism, where Einstein was a pronounced [pacifist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pacifist "Pacifist").[[118]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007373-121) During an address to Caltech's students, Einstein noted that science was often inclined to do more harm than good.[[119]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007374-122)

This aversion to war also led Einstein to befriend author [Upton Sinclair](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Upton_Sinclair "Upton Sinclair") and film star [Charlie Chaplin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charlie_Chaplin "Charlie Chaplin"), both noted for their pacifism. [Carl Laemmle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carl_Laemmle "Carl Laemmle"), head of [Universal Studios](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_Pictures "Universal Pictures"), gave Einstein a tour of his studio and introduced him to Chaplin. They had an instant rapport, with Chaplin inviting Einstein and his wife, Elsa, to his home for dinner. Chaplin said Einstein's outward persona, calm and gentle, seemed to conceal a "highly emotional temperament", from which came his "extraordinary intellectual energy".[[120]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChaplin1964320-123)

Chaplin's film _[City Lights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/City\_Lights "City Lights")_ was to premiere a few days later in Hollywood, and Chaplin invited Einstein and Elsa to join him as his special guests. [Walter Isaacson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Walter_Isaacson "Walter Isaacson"), Einstein's biographer, described this as one of the most memorable scenes in the new era of celebrity.[[119]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007374-122) Chaplin visited Einstein at his home on a later trip to Berlin and recalled his "modest little flat" and the piano at which he had begun writing his theory. Chaplin speculated that it was possibly used as kindling wood by the Nazis.[[121]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChaplin1964322-124) Einstein and Chaplin were cheered at the premiere of the film. Chaplin said to Einstein, "They cheer me because they understand me, and they cheer you because no one understands you."[[119]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007374-122)

### Emigration to the US (1933)

[![Image 20: Cartoon of Einstein, who has shed his "Pacifism" wings, standing next to a pillar labeled "World Peace". He is rolling up his sleeves and holding a sword labeled "Preparedness".](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Einstein-cartoon1.jpg/250px-Einstein-cartoon1.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Einstein-cartoon1.jpg)

Cartoon of Einstein after shedding his "pacifism" wings ([Charles R. Macauley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_R._Macauley "Charles R. Macauley"), c. 1933)

In February 1933, while on a visit to the United States, Einstein knew he could not return to Germany with the rise to power of the [Nazis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_Germany "Nazi Germany") under Germany's new chancellor, [Adolf Hitler](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adolf_Hitler "Adolf Hitler").[[122]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEF%C3%B6lsing1997659-125)[[123]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007404-126)

While at American universities in early 1933, he undertook his third two-month visiting professorship at the [California Institute of Technology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_Institute_of_Technology "California Institute of Technology") in Pasadena. In February and March 1933, the [Gestapo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gestapo "Gestapo") repeatedly raided his family's apartment in Berlin.[[124]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-127) He and his wife Elsa returned to Europe in March, and during the trip, they learned that the German Reichstag had passed the [Enabling Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Enabling_Act_of_1933 "Enabling Act of 1933") on 23 March, transforming Hitler's government into a _de facto_ legal dictatorship, and that they would not be able to proceed to Berlin. Later on, they heard that their cottage had been raided by the Nazis and Einstein's personal sailboat confiscated. Upon landing in [Antwerp](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antwerp "Antwerp"), Belgium on 28 March, Einstein immediately went to the German consulate and surrendered his passport, formally renouncing his German citizenship.[[125]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007405-128) The Nazis later sold his boat and converted his cottage into a [Hitler Youth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hitler_Youth "Hitler Youth") camp.[[126]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-el4GB-129)

#### Refugee status

[![Image 21](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Einstein%27s_landing_card_%285706142737%29.jpg/250px-Einstein%27s_landing_card_%285706142737%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Einstein%27s_landing_card_(5706142737).jpg)

Landing card for Einstein's 26 May 1933 arrival in [Dover](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dover "Dover"), England from [Ostend](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ostend "Ostend"), Belgium,[[127]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-robinson19-130) enroute to [Oxford](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxford "Oxford")[[128]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-robinson24-131)

In April 1933, Einstein discovered that the new German government had passed [laws barring Jews from holding any official positions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Law_for_the_Restoration_of_the_Professional_Civil_Service "Law for the Restoration of the Professional Civil Service"), including teaching at universities.[[129]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007407%E2%80%93410-132) Historian [Gerald Holton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gerald_Holton "Gerald Holton") describes how, with virtually no audible protest being raised by their colleagues, thousands of Jewish scientists were suddenly forced to give up their university positions and their names were removed from the rolls of institutions where they were employed.[[130]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHolton1984-133)

A month later, Einstein's works were among those targeted by the [German Student Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_Student_Union "German Student Union") in the [Nazi book burnings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_book_burnings "Nazi book burnings"), with Nazi propaganda minister [Joseph Goebbels](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Goebbels "Joseph Goebbels") proclaiming, "Jewish intellectualism is dead." One German magazine included him in a list of enemies of the German regime with the phrase, "not yet hanged", offering a $5,000 bounty on his head.[[129]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007407%E2%80%93410-132)[[131]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Jerome-134) In a subsequent letter to physicist and friend [Max Born](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Max_Born "Max Born"), who had already emigrated from Germany to England, Einstein wrote, ...I must confess that the degree of their brutality and cowardice came as something of a surprise.[[129]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007407%E2%80%93410-132) After moving to the US, he described the book burnings as a spontaneous emotional outburst by those who shun popular enlightenment, and more than anything else in the world, fear the influence of men of intellectual independence.[[132]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-135)

Einstein was now without a permanent home, unsure where he would live and work, and equally worried about the fate of countless other scientists still in Germany. Aided by the [Academic Assistance Council](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Academic_Assistance_Council "Academic Assistance Council"), founded in April 1933 by British Liberal politician [William Beveridge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Beveridge "William Beveridge") to help academics escape Nazi persecution, Einstein was able to leave Germany.[[133]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Albert_Hall-136) He rented a house in De Haan, Belgium, where he lived for a few months. In late July 1933, he visited England for about six weeks at the invitation of the British Member of Parliament Commander [Oliver Locker-Lampson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oliver_Locker-Lampson "Oliver Locker-Lampson"), who had become friends with him in the preceding years.[[127]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-robinson19-130) Locker-Lampson invited him to stay near his [Cromer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cromer "Cromer") home in a secluded wooden cabin on Roughton Heath in the Parish of [Roughton, Norfolk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roughton,_Norfolk "Roughton, Norfolk"). To protect Einstein, Locker-Lampson had two bodyguards watch over him; a photo of them carrying shotguns and guarding Einstein was published in the _Daily Herald_ on 24 July 1933.[[134]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007422-137)[[135]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-3zIp7-138)

[![Image 22](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Churchill_and_Einstein_in_1933.jpg/250px-Churchill_and_Einstein_in_1933.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Churchill_and_Einstein_in_1933.jpg)

[Winston Churchill](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Winston_Churchill "Winston Churchill") and Einstein at [Chartwell](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chartwell "Chartwell") House, 31 May 1933

Locker-Lampson took Einstein to meet [Winston Churchill](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Winston_Churchill "Winston Churchill") at his home, and later, [Austen Chamberlain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Austen_Chamberlain "Austen Chamberlain") and former Prime Minister [Lloyd George](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lloyd_George "Lloyd George").[[136]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007419%E2%80%93420-139) Einstein asked them to help bring Jewish scientists out of Germany. British historian [Martin Gilbert](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Martin_Gilbert "Martin Gilbert") notes that Churchill responded immediately, and sent his friend physicist [Frederick Lindemann](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frederick_Lindemann "Frederick Lindemann") to Germany to seek out Jewish scientists and place them in British universities.[[137]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Gilbert-140) Churchill later observed that as a result of Germany having driven the Jews out, they had lowered their "technical standards" and put [the Allies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II "Allies of World War II")' technology ahead of theirs.[[137]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Gilbert-140)

Einstein later contacted leaders of other nations, including Turkey's Prime Minister, [İsmet İnönü](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C4%B0smet_%C4%B0n%C3%B6n%C3%BC "İsmet İnönü"), to whom he wrote in September 1933, requesting placement of unemployed German-Jewish scientists. As a result of Einstein's letter, Jewish invitees to Turkey eventually totaled over "1,000 saved individuals".[[138]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-aDu8s-141)

Locker-Lampson also submitted a bill to parliament to extend British citizenship to Einstein, during which period Einstein made a number of public appearances describing the crisis brewing in Europe.[[139]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClark1971-142) In one of his speeches he denounced Germany's treatment of Jews, while at the same time he introduced a bill promoting Jewish citizenship in Palestine, as they were being denied citizenship elsewhere.[[140]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-AP-143) In his speech he described Einstein as a "citizen of the world" who should be offered a temporary shelter in the UK.[[note 3]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-gnriE-144)[[141]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Guardian-145) Both bills failed, however, and Einstein then accepted an earlier offer from the [Institute for Advanced Study](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Institute_for_Advanced_Study "Institute for Advanced Study"), in [Princeton, New Jersey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Princeton,_New_Jersey "Princeton, New Jersey"), US, to become a resident scholar.[[139]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClark1971-142)

#### Resident scholar at the Institute for Advanced Study

[![Image 23](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Einstein-formal_portrait-35_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Einstein-formal_portrait-35_%28cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Einstein-formal_portrait-35_(cropped).jpg)

Portrait of Einstein taken in 1935 at [Princeton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Princeton_University "Princeton University")

On 3 October 1933, Einstein delivered a speech on the importance of academic freedom before a packed audience at the [Royal Albert Hall](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Royal_Albert_Hall "Royal Albert Hall") in London, with _[The Times](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Times "The Times")_ reporting he was wildly cheered throughout.[[133]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Albert_Hall-136) Four days later he returned to the US and took up a position at the [Institute for Advanced Study](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Institute_for_Advanced_Study "Institute for Advanced Study"),[[139]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClark1971-142)[[142]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEF%C3%B6lsing1997649,_678-146) noted for having become a refuge for scientists fleeing [Nazi Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_Germany "Nazi Germany").[[143]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Arntzenius2011-147) At the time, most American universities, including Harvard, Princeton and Yale, had minimal or no Jewish faculty or students, as a result of their [Jewish quotas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_quota "Jewish quota"), which lasted until the late 1940s.[[143]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Arntzenius2011-147)

Einstein was still undecided about his future. He had offers from several European universities, including [Christ Church, Oxford](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christ_Church,_Oxford "Christ Church, Oxford"), where he stayed for three short periods between May 1931 and June 1933[[128]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-robinson24-131) and was offered a five-year research [fellowship](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fellowship "Fellowship") (called a "[studentship](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Studentship "Studentship")" at Christ Church),[[144]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FFt5E-148)[[145]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-v8v06-149) but in 1935, he arrived at the decision to remain permanently in the United States and apply for citizenship.[[139]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClark1971-142)[[146]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEF%C3%B6lsing1997686%E2%80%93687-150)

Einstein's affiliation with the Institute for Advanced Study would last until his death in 1955.[[147]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-mzNc5-151) He was one of the four first selected (along with [John von Neumann](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann "John von Neumann"), [Kurt Gödel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurt_G%C3%B6del "Kurt Gödel") and [Hermann Weyl](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hermann_Weyl "Hermann Weyl")[[148]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-152)) at the new Institute. He soon developed a close friendship with Gödel; the two would take long walks together discussing their work. [Bruria Kaufman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bruria_Kaufman "Bruria Kaufman"), his assistant, later became a physicist. During this period, Einstein tried to develop a [unified field theory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unified_field_theory "Unified field theory") and to refute the [accepted interpretation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Copenhagen_interpretation "Copenhagen interpretation") of [quantum physics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_physics "Quantum physics"), both unsuccessfully. He lived in Princeton at his home from 1935 onwards. The [Albert Einstein House](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein_House "Albert Einstein House") was made a [National Historic Landmark](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Historic_Landmark "National Historic Landmark") in 1976.

#### World War II and the Manhattan Project

[![Image 24](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Einstein-Roosevelt-letter.png/500px-Einstein-Roosevelt-letter.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Einstein-Roosevelt-letter.png)
