Facsimile of the [Einstein–Szilard letter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Einstein%E2%80%93Szilard_letter "Einstein–Szilard letter")

In 1939, a group of Hungarian scientists that included émigré physicist [Leó Szilárd](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Le%C3%B3_Szil%C3%A1rd "Leó Szilárd") attempted to alert [Washington, D.C.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Washington,_D.C. "Washington, D.C.") to ongoing Nazi atomic bomb research. The group's warnings were discounted. Einstein and Szilárd, along with other refugees such as [Edward Teller](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edward_Teller "Edward Teller") and [Eugene Wigner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eugene_Wigner "Eugene Wigner"), regarded it as their responsibility to alert Americans to the possibility that German scientists might win the [race to build an atomic bomb](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_nuclear_energy_project "German nuclear energy project"), and to warn that Hitler would be more than willing to resort to such a weapon.[[149]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007630-153)[[150]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-o4fkQ-154) To make certain the US was aware of the danger, in July 1939, a few months before the beginning of World War II in Europe, Szilárd and Wigner visited Einstein to explain the possibility of atomic bombs, which Einstein, a pacifist, said he had never considered.[[151]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-pRqWK-155) He was asked to lend his support by writing [a letter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Einstein%E2%80%93Szilard_letter "Einstein–Szilard letter"), with Szilárd, to President [Franklin D. Roosevelt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt "Franklin D. Roosevelt"), recommending the US pay attention and engage in its own nuclear weapons research.

The letter is believed to be arguably the key stimulus for the U.S. adoption of serious investigations into nuclear weapons on the eve of the U.S. entry into World War II.[[152]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-4Z68g-156) In addition to the letter, Einstein used his connections with the [Belgian royal family](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Belgian_royal_family "Belgian royal family")[[153]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-eZym8-157) and the Belgian queen mother to get access with a personal envoy to the White House's Oval Office. Some say that as a result of Einstein's letter and his meetings with Roosevelt, the US entered the "race" to develop the bomb, drawing on its "immense material, financial, and scientific resources" to initiate the [Manhattan Project](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manhattan_Project "Manhattan Project").

For Einstein, war was a disease... [and] he called for resistance to war. By signing the letter to Roosevelt, some argue he went against his pacifist principles.[[154]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-z73PK-158) In 1954, a year before his death, Einstein said to his old friend, [Linus Pauling](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linus_Pauling "Linus Pauling"), I made one great mistake in my life—when I signed the letter to President Roosevelt recommending that atom bombs be made; but there was some justification—the danger that the Germans would make them...[[155]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClark1971752-159) In 1955, Einstein and ten other intellectuals and scientists, including British philosopher [Bertrand Russell](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bertrand_Russell "Bertrand Russell"), signed [a manifesto](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russell%E2%80%93Einstein_Manifesto "Russell–Einstein Manifesto") highlighting the danger of nuclear weapons.[[156]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-160) In 1960 Einstein was included posthumously as a charter member of the [World Academy of Art and Science](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Academy_of_Art_and_Science "World Academy of Art and Science") (WAAS),[[157]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-161) an organization founded by distinguished scientists and intellectuals who committed themselves to the responsible and ethical advances of science, particularly in light of the development of nuclear weapons.

#### US citizenship

[![Image 25](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Citizen-Einstein.jpg/250px-Citizen-Einstein.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Citizen-Einstein.jpg)

Einstein accepting a [US citizenship](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Citizenship_of_the_United_States "Citizenship of the United States") certificate from judge [Phillip Forman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phillip_Forman "Phillip Forman") in 1940

Einstein became an American citizen in 1940. Not long after settling into his career at the Institute for Advanced Study in Princeton, New Jersey, he expressed his appreciation of the [meritocracy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Meritocracy "Meritocracy") in American culture compared to Europe. He recognized the "right of individuals to say and think what they pleased" without social barriers. As a result, individuals were encouraged, he said, to be more creative, a trait he valued from his early education.[[158]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007432-162)

Einstein joined the [National Association for the Advancement of Colored People](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Association_for_the_Advancement_of_Colored_People "National Association for the Advancement of Colored People") (NAACP) in Princeton, where he campaigned for the [civil rights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civil_rights_movement_(1896%E2%80%931954) "Civil rights movement (1896–1954)") of African Americans. He considered racism America's "worst disease",[[131]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Jerome-134)[[159]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-smithsonianmag-163) seeing it as handed down from one generation to the next.[[160]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalaprice2005148%E2%80%93149-164) As part of his involvement, he corresponded with civil rights activist [W. E. B. Du Bois](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/W._E._B._Du_Bois "W. E. B. Du Bois") and was prepared to testify on his behalf during his trial as an alleged foreign agent in 1951.[[161]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobeson2002565-165) When Einstein offered to be a character witness for Du Bois, the judge decided to drop the case.[[162]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-civil-166)

In 1946, Einstein visited [Lincoln University](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lincoln_University_(Pennsylvania) "Lincoln University (Pennsylvania)") in Pennsylvania, a [historically black college](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Historically_black_college "Historically black college"), where he was awarded an honorary degree. Lincoln was the first university in the United States to grant college degrees to African Americans; alumni include [Langston Hughes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Langston_Hughes "Langston Hughes") and [Thurgood Marshall](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thurgood_Marshall "Thurgood Marshall"). Einstein gave a speech about racism in America, adding, I do not intend to be quiet about it.[[163]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Jerome_Isis-167) A resident of Princeton recalls that Einstein had once paid the college tuition for a black student.[[162]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-civil-166) Einstein has said, Being a Jew myself, perhaps I can understand and empathize with how black people feel as victims of discrimination.[[159]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-smithsonianmag-163) Isaacson writes that "When [Marian Anderson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marian_Anderson "Marian Anderson"), the black contralto, came to Princeton for a concert in 1937, the Nassau Inn refused her a room. So Einstein invited her to stay at his house on Main Street, in what was a deeply personal as well as symbolic gesture ... Whenever she returned to Princeton, she stayed with Einstein, her last visit coming just two months before he died."[[164]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007445-168)

### Personal views

#### Political views

[![Image 26: Casual group shot of four men and two women standing on a brick pavement.](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Einstein_Apr.1921_SS_Rotterdam_32099.jpg/250px-Einstein_Apr.1921_SS_Rotterdam_32099.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Einstein_Apr.1921_SS_Rotterdam_32099.jpg)

Albert Einstein and [Elsa Einstein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elsa_Einstein "Elsa Einstein") arriving in New York in 1921. Accompanying them are Zionist leaders [Chaim Weizmann](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chaim_Weizmann "Chaim Weizmann") (future president of Israel), Weizmann's wife [Vera Weizmann](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vera_Weizmann "Vera Weizmann"), [Menahem Ussishkin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Menahem_Ussishkin "Menahem Ussishkin"), and Ben-Zion Mossinson.

In 1918, Einstein was one of the signatories of the founding proclamation of the [German Democratic Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_Democratic_Party "German Democratic Party"), a liberal party.[[165]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-169)[[166]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-170) Later in his life, Einstein's political view was in favor of [socialism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialism "Socialism") and critical of capitalism, which he detailed in his essays such as "[Why Socialism?](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Why_Socialism%3F "Why Socialism?")".[[167]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-171)[[168]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-LXsUJ-172) His opinions on the [Bolsheviks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bolsheviks "Bolsheviks") also changed with time. In 1925, he criticized them for not having a "well-regulated system of government" and called their rule a "regime of terror and a tragedy in human history". He later adopted a more moderated view, criticizing their methods but praising them, which is shown by his 1929 remark on [Vladimir Lenin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin "Vladimir Lenin"):

> In Lenin I honor a man, who in total sacrifice of his own person has committed his entire energy to realizing social justice. I do not find his methods advisable. One thing is certain, however: men like him are the guardians and renewers of mankind's conscience.[[169]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoweSchulmann2013[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid_X1dAAAAQBAJpg413_412,_413]-173)

Einstein offered and was called on to give judgments and opinions on matters often unrelated to theoretical physics or mathematics.[[139]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClark1971-142) He strongly advocated the idea of a democratic [global government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_government "Global government") that would check the power of nation-states in the framework of a world federation.[[170]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007487,_494,_550-174) He wrote I advocate world government because I am convinced that there is no other possible way of eliminating the most terrible danger in which man has ever found himself.[[171]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-175) The FBI created a secret dossier on Einstein in 1932; by the time of his death, it was 1,427 pages long.[[172]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-ixWWZ-176)

Einstein was deeply impressed by [Mahatma Gandhi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mahatma_Gandhi "Mahatma Gandhi"), with whom he corresponded. He described Gandhi as a role model for the generations to come.[[173]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Albano-M%C3%BCller-177) The initial connection was established on 27 September 1931, when [Wilfrid Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wilfrid_Israel "Wilfrid Israel") took his Indian guest [V. A. Sundaram](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/V._A._Sundaram "V. A. Sundaram") to meet his friend Einstein at his summer home in the town of Caputh. Sundaram was Gandhi's disciple and special envoy, whom Wilfrid Israel met while visiting India and visiting the Indian leader's home in 1925. During the visit, Einstein wrote a short letter to Gandhi that was delivered to him through his envoy, and Gandhi responded quickly with his own letter. Although in the end Einstein and Gandhi were unable to meet as they had hoped, the direct connection between them was established through Wilfrid Israel.[[174]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-178)

#### Relationship with Zionism

Einstein was a figurehead leader in the establishment of the [Hebrew University of Jerusalem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hebrew_University_of_Jerusalem "Hebrew University of Jerusalem"),[[175]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-179) which opened in 1925.[[176]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-180) Earlier, in 1921, he was asked by the biochemist and president of the [World Zionist Organization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Zionist_Organization "World Zionist Organization"), [Chaim Weizmann](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chaim_Weizmann "Chaim Weizmann"), to help raise funds for the planned university.[[177]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007290-181) He made suggestions for the creation of an Institute of Agriculture, a Chemical Institute and an Institute of Microbiology in order to fight the various ongoing epidemics such as [malaria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malaria "Malaria"), which he called an "evil" that was undermining a third of the country's development.[[178]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoweSchulmann2007161-182) He also promoted the establishment of an Oriental Studies Institute, to include language courses given in both [Hebrew](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hebrew "Hebrew") and [Arabic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabic "Arabic").[[179]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoweSchulmann2007158-183)

Einstein was not a [nationalist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nationalist "Nationalist") and opposed the creation of an independent Jewish state.[[180]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoweSchulmann200733-184) He felt that the waves of arriving Jews of the [Aliyah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aliyah "Aliyah") could live alongside existing Arabs in [Palestine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestine_(region) "Palestine (region)"). The state of [Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel "Israel") was established without his help in 1948; Einstein was limited to a marginal role in the [Zionist movement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zionism "Zionism").[[181]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-185) Upon the death of Israeli president Weizmann in November 1952, Prime Minister [David Ben-Gurion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Ben-Gurion "David Ben-Gurion") offered Einstein the largely ceremonial position of [President of Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/President_of_Israel "President of Israel") at the urging of [Ezriel Carlebach](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ezriel_Carlebach "Ezriel Carlebach").[[182]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Time-186)[[183]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Msb2q-187) The offer was presented by Israel's ambassador in Washington, [Abba Eban](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abba_Eban "Abba Eban"), who explained that the offer embodies the deepest respect which the Jewish people can repose in any of its sons. Einstein wrote that he was "deeply moved", but "at once saddened and ashamed" that he could not accept it.[[184]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007522-188)

#### Religious and philosophical views

Opening of Einstein's speech (11 April 1943) for the United Jewish Appeal (recording by Radio Universidad Nacional de La Plata, Argentina) 

* * *

Ladies (coughs) and gentlemen, our age is proud of the progress it has made in man's intellectual development. The search and striving for truth and knowledge is one of the highest of man's qualities...

Per [Lee Smolin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lee_Smolin "Lee Smolin"), I believe what allowed Einstein to achieve so much was primarily a moral quality. He simply cared far more than most of his colleagues that the laws of physics have to explain everything in nature coherently and consistently.[[185]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007549%E2%80%93550-189) Einstein expounded his spiritual outlook in a wide array of writings and interviews.[[186]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-018QJ-190) He said he had sympathy for the impersonal [pantheistic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pantheistic "Pantheistic") God of [Baruch Spinoza's philosophy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spinozism "Spinozism").[[187]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidG_iziBAPXtECpgPA325_325]-191) He did not believe in a [personal god](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Personal_god "Personal god") who concerns himself with fates and actions of human beings, a view which he described as naïve.[[188]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalaprice2000218-192) He clarified, however, that I am not an atheist,[[189]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007390-193) preferring to call himself an agnostic,[[190]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalaprice2010[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidG_iziBAPXtECpgPA340_340]-194)[[191]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-flickr2687-195) or a deeply religious nonbeliever.[[188]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalaprice2000218-192) He wrote that A spirit is manifest in the laws of the universe—a spirit vastly superior to that of man, and one in the face of which we with our modest powers must feel humble. In this way the pursuit of science leads to a religious feeling of a special sort.[[192]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007550%E2%80%93551-196)

Einstein was primarily affiliated with non-religious [humanist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Secular_humanist "Secular humanist") and [Ethical Culture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethical_Culture "Ethical Culture") groups in both the UK and US. He served on the advisory board of the [First Humanist Society of New York](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Humanist_Society_of_New_York "First Humanist Society of New York"),[[193]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-mKToJ-197) and was an honorary associate of the [Rationalist Association](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rationalist_Association "Rationalist Association"), which publishes _[New Humanist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New\_Humanist "New Humanist")_ in Britain. For the 75th anniversary of the [New York Society for Ethical Culture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_Society_for_Ethical_Culture "New York Society for Ethical Culture"), he stated that the idea of Ethical Culture embodied his personal conception of what is most valuable and enduring in religious idealism. He observed, Without 'ethical culture' there is no salvation for humanity.[[194]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-198)

In a German-language letter to philosopher [Eric Gutkind](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eric_Gutkind "Eric Gutkind"), dated 3 January 1954, Einstein wrote:

> [The word God](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/God_(word) "God (word)") is for me nothing more than the expression and product of human weaknesses, the Bible a collection of honorable, but still primitive legends which are nevertheless pretty childish. No interpretation no matter how subtle can (for me) change this. ... For me the [Jewish religion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_religion "Jewish religion") like all other religions is an incarnation of the most childish superstitions. And the [Jewish people](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_people "Jewish people") to whom I gladly belong and with whose mentality I have a deep affinity have no different quality for me than all other people. ... I cannot see anything '[chosen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jews_as_the_chosen_people "Jews as the chosen people")' about them.[[195]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-xI99y-199)

Einstein had been sympathetic toward vegetarianism for a long time. In a letter in 1930 to Hermann Huth, vice-president of the [German Vegetarian Federation (Deutsche Vegetarier-Bund)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ProVeg_Deutschland#History "ProVeg Deutschland"), he wrote:

> Although I have been prevented by outward circumstances from observing a strictly vegetarian diet, I have long been an adherent to the cause in principle. Besides agreeing with the aims of vegetarianism for aesthetic and moral reasons, it is my view that a vegetarian manner of living by its purely physical effect on the human temperament would most beneficially influence the lot of mankind.[[196]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-200)

He became a vegetarian himself only during the last part of his life. In March 1954 he wrote in a letter: So I am living without fats, without meat, without fish, but am feeling quite well this way. It almost seems to me that man was not born to be a carnivore.[[197]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-201)

#### Love of music

[![Image 27](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Wanda_von_Debschitz-Kunowski_Albert_Einstein_beim_Geigenspiel_1927.jpg/330px-Wanda_von_Debschitz-Kunowski_Albert_Einstein_beim_Geigenspiel_1927.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Wanda_von_Debschitz-Kunowski_Albert_Einstein_beim_Geigenspiel_1927.jpg)

Einstein playing the violin, 1927

Einstein developed an appreciation for music at an early age. In his late journals he wrote:

> If I were not a physicist, I would probably be a musician. I often think in music. I live my daydreams in music. I see my life in terms of music... I get most joy in life out of music.[[198]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-BQH5A-202)[[199]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-aBOjz-203)

His mother played the piano reasonably well and wanted her son to learn the violin, not only to instill in him a love of music but also to help him assimilate into [German culture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_culture "German culture"). According to conductor [Leon Botstein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Botstein "Leon Botstein"), Einstein began playing when he was 5. However, he did not enjoy it at that age.[[200]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Botstein-204)

When he turned 13, he discovered [Mozart](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mozart "Mozart")'s [violin sonatas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mozart_violin_sonatas "Mozart violin sonatas"), whereupon he became enamored of Mozart's compositions and studied music more willingly. Einstein taught himself to play without "ever practicing systematically". He said that love is a better teacher than a sense of duty.[[200]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Botstein-204) At the age of 17, he was heard by a school examiner in Aarau while playing [Beethoven](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beethoven "Beethoven")'s [violin sonatas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beethoven%27s_violin_sonatas_(disambiguation) "Beethoven's violin sonatas (disambiguation)"). The examiner stated afterward that his playing was remarkable and revealing of 'great insight'. What struck the examiner, writes Botstein, was that Einstein displayed a deep love of the music, a quality that was and remains in short supply. Music possessed an unusual meaning for this student.[[200]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Botstein-204)

Music took on a pivotal and permanent role in Einstein's life from that period on. Although the idea of becoming a professional musician himself was not on his mind at any time, among those with whom Einstein played [chamber music](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chamber_music "Chamber music") were a few professionals, including Kurt Appelbaum, and he performed for private audiences and friends. Chamber music had also become a regular part of his social life while living in Bern, Zurich, and Berlin, where he played with Max Planck and his son, among others. He is sometimes erroneously credited as the editor of the 1937 edition of the [Köchel catalog](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/K%C3%B6chel_catalog "Köchel catalog") of Mozart's work; that edition was prepared by [Alfred Einstein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alfred_Einstein "Alfred Einstein"), who may have been a distant relation.[[201]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-kGuWC-205)[[202]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-OIn6p-206) Mozart was a special favorite; he said that "Mozart's music is so pure it seems to have been ever-present in the universe." He preferred [Bach](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bach "Bach") to Beethoven: "Give me Bach, rather, and then more Bach."[[203]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson200738-207)

In 1931, while engaged in research at the California Institute of Technology, he visited the Zoellner family conservatory in Los Angeles, where he played some of Beethoven and Mozart's works with members of the [Zoellner Quartet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zoellner_Quartet "Zoellner Quartet").[[204]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Times-208)[[205]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-RR-209) Near the end of his life, when the young [Juilliard Quartet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Juilliard_Quartet "Juilliard Quartet") visited him in Princeton, he played his violin with them, and the quartet was impressed by Einstein's level of coordination and intonation.[[200]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Botstein-204)

### Death

On 17 April 1955, Einstein experienced [internal bleeding](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internal_bleeding "Internal bleeding") caused by the rupture of an [abdominal aortic aneurysm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdominal_aortic_aneurysm "Abdominal aortic aneurysm"), which had previously been reinforced surgically by [Rudolph Nissen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rudolph_Nissen "Rudolph Nissen") in 1948.[[206]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-BXLfp-210) He took the draft of a speech he was preparing for a television appearance commemorating the state of Israel's seventh anniversary with him to the hospital, but he did not live to complete it.[[207]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-QN45b-211)

Einstein refused surgery, saying, I want to go when I want. It is tasteless to prolong life artificially. I have done my share; it is time to go. I will do it elegantly.[[208]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-BhiNM-212) He died in the [Princeton Hospital](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Princeton_Hospital "Princeton Hospital") early the next morning at the age of 76, having continued to work until near the end.[[209]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-YUhsl-213)

During the autopsy, the pathologist [Thomas Stoltz Harvey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_Stoltz_Harvey "Thomas Stoltz Harvey") removed [Einstein's brain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Einstein%27s_brain "Einstein's brain") for preservation without the permission of his family, in the hope that the [neuroscience](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neuroscience "Neuroscience") of the future would be able to discover what made Einstein so intelligent.[[210]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-MqyYW-214) Einstein's remains were cremated in [Trenton, New Jersey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trenton,_New_Jersey "Trenton, New Jersey"),[[211]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-215) and his ashes were scattered at an undisclosed location.[[212]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-GQrBZ-216)[[213]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Obit-217)

In a memorial lecture delivered on 13 December 1965 at [UNESCO](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UNESCO "UNESCO") headquarters, nuclear physicist [J. Robert Oppenheimer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/J._Robert_Oppenheimer "J. Robert Oppenheimer") summarized his [impression of Einstein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Einstein%E2%80%93Oppenheimer_relationship "Einstein–Oppenheimer relationship") as a person: He was almost wholly without sophistication and wholly without worldliness... There was always with him a wonderful purity at once childlike and profoundly stubborn.[[214]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-aJHxn-218)

Einstein bequeathed his personal archives, library, and intellectual assets to the [Hebrew University of Jerusalem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hebrew_University_of_Jerusalem "Hebrew University of Jerusalem") in Israel.[[215]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-219)

Scientific career
-----------------

Throughout his life, Einstein published hundreds of books and articles.[[15]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Bio-17)[[216]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Paul_Arthur_Schilpp,_editor_1951_730%E2%80%93746-220) He published more than 300 scientific papers and 150 non-scientific ones.[[11]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Nobel-13)[[216]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Paul_Arthur_Schilpp,_editor_1951_730%E2%80%93746-220) On 5 December 2014, universities and archives announced the release of Einstein's papers, comprising more than 30,000 unique documents.[[217]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-221)[[218]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-NYT-20141204-DB-222) In addition to the work he did by himself he also collaborated with other scientists on additional projects including the [Bose–Einstein statistics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bose%E2%80%93Einstein_statistics "Bose–Einstein statistics"), the [Einstein refrigerator](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Einstein_refrigerator "Einstein refrigerator") and others.[[219]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Instituut-Lorentz-223)[[220]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-e5xd8-224)

### Statistical mechanics

#### Thermodynamic fluctuations and statistical physics

Einstein's first paper[[75]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Einstein_1901-78)[[221]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-PubList-225) submitted in 1900 to _[Annalen der Physik](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Annalen\_der\_Physik "Annalen der Physik")_ was on [capillary attraction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capillary_attraction "Capillary attraction"). It was published in 1901 with the title "Folgerungen aus den Capillaritätserscheinungen", which translates as "Conclusions from the capillarity phenomena". Two papers he published in 1902–1903 (thermodynamics) attempted to interpret [atomic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atom "Atom") phenomena from a statistical point of view. These papers were the foundation for the 1905 paper on Brownian motion, which showed that Brownian movement can be construed as firm evidence that molecules exist. His research in 1903 and 1904 was mainly concerned with the effect of finite atomic size on diffusion phenomena.[[221]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-PubList-225)

#### Theory of critical opalescence

Einstein returned to the problem of thermodynamic fluctuations, giving a treatment of the density variations in a fluid at its critical point. Ordinarily the density fluctuations are controlled by the second derivative of the free energy with respect to the density. At the critical point, this derivative is zero, leading to large fluctuations. The effect of density fluctuations is that light of all wavelengths is scattered, making the fluid look milky white. Einstein relates this to [Rayleigh scattering](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rayleigh_scattering "Rayleigh scattering"), which is what happens when the fluctuation size is much smaller than the wavelength, and which explains why the sky is blue.[[222]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-L2N73-226) Einstein quantitatively derived critical opalescence from a treatment of density fluctuations, and demonstrated how both the effect and Rayleigh scattering originate from the atomistic constitution of matter.

### 1905 – _Annus Mirabilis_ papers

The [_Annus Mirabilis_ papers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Annus_mirabilis_papers "Annus mirabilis papers") are four articles pertaining to the photoelectric effect (which gave rise to [quantum theory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_mechanics "Quantum mechanics")), [Brownian motion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brownian_motion "Brownian motion"), the [special theory of relativity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special_theory_of_relativity "Special theory of relativity"), and [_E_=_mc_ 2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mass%E2%80%93energy_equivalence "Mass–energy equivalence") that Einstein published in the _Annalen der Physik_ scientific journal in 1905. These four works contributed substantially to the foundation of [modern physics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modern_physics "Modern physics") and changed views on [space](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space "Space"), time, and [matter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Matter "Matter"). The four papers are:

| Title (translated) | Area of focus | Received | Published | Significance |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| "On a Heuristic Viewpoint Concerning the Production and Transformation of Light"[[223]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-1905a-227) | Photoelectric effect | 18 March | 9 June | Resolved an unsolved puzzle by suggesting that energy is exchanged only in discrete amounts ([quanta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum "Quantum")).[[224]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-1Jhcb-228) This idea was pivotal to the early development of quantum theory.[[225]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-oJBvd-229) |
| "On the Motion of Small Particles Suspended in a Stationary Liquid, as Required by the Molecular Kinetic Theory of Heat"[[226]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-230) | [Brownian motion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brownian_motion "Brownian motion") | 11 May | 18 July | Explained empirical evidence for the [atomic theory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atomic_theory "Atomic theory"), supporting the application of [statistical physics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistical_physics "Statistical physics"). |
| "On the Electrodynamics of Moving Bodies"[[227]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-1905d-231) | [Special relativity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special_relativity "Special relativity") | 30 June | 26 September | Reconciled [Maxwell](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_Clerk_Maxwell "James Clerk Maxwell")'s equations for electricity and magnetism with the laws of mechanics by introducing changes to mechanics, resulting from analysis based on the independence of the speed of light from the motion of the observer.[[228]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-RhZ8x-232) Discredited the concept of a "[luminiferous ether](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luminiferous_ether "Luminiferous ether")".[[229]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-lhfJ9-233) |
| "Does the Inertia of a Body Depend Upon Its Energy Content?"[[230]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-234) | [Matter–energy equivalence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mass%E2%80%93energy_equivalence "Mass–energy equivalence") | 27 September | 21 November | Equivalence of matter and energy, _E_=_mc_ 2, the existence of "[rest energy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rest_energy "Rest energy")", and the basis of nuclear energy. |

### Special relativity

Einstein's "_Zur Elektrodynamik bewegter Körper_"[[227]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-1905d-231) ("On the Electrodynamics of Moving Bodies") was received on 30 June 1905 and published 26 September of that same year. It reconciled conflicts between [Maxwell's equations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maxwell%27s_equations "Maxwell's equations") (the laws of electricity and magnetism) and the laws of Newtonian mechanics by introducing changes to the laws of mechanics.[[231]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEF%C3%B6lsing1997178%E2%80%93198-235) Observationally, the effects of these changes are most apparent at high speeds (where objects are moving at speeds close to the [speed of light](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Speed_of_light "Speed of light")). The theory developed in this paper later became known as Einstein's special theory of relativity.

This paper predicted that, when measured in the frame of a relatively moving observer, a clock carried by a moving body would appear to [slow down](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Time_dilation "Time dilation"), and the body itself would [contract](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Length_contraction "Length contraction") in its direction of motion. This paper also argued that the idea of a [luminiferous aether](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luminiferous_aether "Luminiferous aether")—one of the leading theoretical entities in physics at the time—was superfluous.[[note 4]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-aBfxO-236)

In his paper on [mass–energy equivalence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mass%E2%80%93energy_equivalence "Mass–energy equivalence"), Einstein produced _E_=_mc_ 2 as a consequence of his special relativity equations.[[232]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStachel2002vi,_15,_90,_131,_[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidOAsQ_hFjhrACpgPA215_215]-237) Einstein's 1905 work on relativity remained controversial for many years, but was accepted by leading physicists, starting with [Max Planck](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Max_Planck "Max Planck").[[note 5]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-sBl2q-238)[[233]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPais1982382%E2%80%93386-239)

Einstein originally framed special relativity in terms of [kinematics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kinematics "Kinematics") (the study of moving bodies). In 1908, [Hermann Minkowski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hermann_Minkowski "Hermann Minkowski") reinterpreted special relativity in geometric terms as a theory of [spacetime](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spacetime "Spacetime"). Einstein adopted Minkowski's formalism in his 1915 [general theory of relativity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_theory_of_relativity "General theory of relativity").[[234]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPais1982151%E2%80%93152-240)

### General relativity

#### General relativity and the equivalence principle

[![Image 28: Black circle covering the sun, rays visible around it, in a dark sky.](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/1919_eclipse_positive.jpg/250px-1919_eclipse_positive.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:1919_eclipse_positive.jpg)

[Eddington](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arthur_Stanley_Eddington "Arthur Stanley Eddington")'s photo of a [solar eclipse](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_eclipse "Solar eclipse")

[General relativity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_relativity "General relativity") (GR) is a [theory of gravitation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theory_of_gravitation "Theory of gravitation") that was developed by Einstein between 1907 and 1915. According to it, the observed gravitational attraction between masses results from the warping of [spacetime](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spacetime "Spacetime") by those masses. General relativity has developed into an essential tool in modern [astrophysics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Astrophysics "Astrophysics"); it provides the foundation for the current understanding of [black holes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_holes "Black holes"), regions of space where gravitational attraction is so strong that not even light can escape.[[235]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-241)

As Einstein later said, the reason for the development of general relativity was that the preference of inertial motions within [special relativity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special_relativity "Special relativity") was unsatisfactory, while a theory which from the outset prefers no state of motion (even accelerated ones) should appear more satisfactory.[[236]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-242) Consequently, in 1907 he published an article on acceleration under special relativity. In that article titled "On the Relativity Principle and the Conclusions Drawn from It", he argued that [free fall](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_fall "Free fall") is really inertial motion, and that for a free-falling observer the rules of special relativity must apply. This argument is called the [equivalence principle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Equivalence_principle "Equivalence principle"). In the same article, Einstein also predicted the phenomena of [gravitational time dilation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gravitational_time_dilation "Gravitational time dilation"), [gravitational redshift](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gravitational_redshift "Gravitational redshift") and [gravitational lensing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gravitational_lensing "Gravitational lensing").[[237]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPais1982179%E2%80%93183-243)[[238]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-244)

In 1911, Einstein published another article "On the Influence of Gravitation on the Propagation of Light" expanding on the 1907 article, in which he estimated the amount of deflection of light by massive bodies. Thus, the theoretical prediction of general relativity could for the first time be tested experimentally.[[239]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPais1982194%E2%80%93195-245)

#### Gravitational waves

In 1916, Einstein predicted [gravitational waves](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gravitational_wave "Gravitational wave"),[[240]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-246)[[241]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-247) ripples in the [curvature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Curvature "Curvature") of spacetime which propagate as [waves](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wave "Wave"), traveling outward from the source, transporting energy as gravitational radiation. The existence of gravitational waves is possible under general relativity due to its [Lorentz invariance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lorentz_invariance "Lorentz invariance") which brings the concept of a finite speed of propagation of the physical interactions of gravity with it. By contrast, gravitational waves cannot exist in the [Newtonian theory of gravitation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Newton%27s_law_of_universal_gravitation "Newton's law of universal gravitation"), which postulates that the physical interactions of gravity propagate at infinite speed.

The first, indirect, detection of gravitational waves came in the 1970s through observation of a pair of closely orbiting [neutron stars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neutron_stars "Neutron stars"), [PSR B1913+16](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PSR_B1913%2B16 "PSR B1913+16").[[242]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-natgeo-248) The explanation for the decay in their orbital period was that they were emitting gravitational waves.[[242]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-natgeo-248)[[243]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Tf1T0-249) Einstein's prediction was confirmed on 11 February 2016, when researchers at [LIGO](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LIGO "LIGO") published the [first observation of gravitational waves](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_observation_of_gravitational_waves "First observation of gravitational waves"),[[244]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-PRL-20160211-250) detected on Earth on 14 September 2015, nearly one hundred years after the prediction.[[242]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-natgeo-248)[[245]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-CO6kH-251)[[246]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-oSmHb-252)[[247]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-hkKSp-253)[[248]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-38Msx-254)

#### Hole argument and Entwurf theory

While developing general relativity, Einstein became confused about the [gauge invariance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gauge_invariance "Gauge invariance") in the theory. He formulated an argument that led him to conclude that a general relativistic field theory is impossible. He gave up looking for fully generally covariant tensor equations and searched for equations that would be invariant under general linear transformations only.[[249]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-255)

In June 1913, the Entwurf ('draft') theory was the result of these investigations. As its name suggests, it was a sketch of a theory, less elegant and more difficult than general relativity, with the equations of motion supplemented by additional gauge fixing conditions. After more than two years of intensive work, Einstein realized that the [hole argument](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hole_argument "Hole argument") was mistaken[[250]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-sOA9t-256) and abandoned the theory in November 1915.

#### Physical cosmology

[![Image 29](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/MillikanLemaitreEinstein.jpg/250px-MillikanLemaitreEinstein.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:MillikanLemaitreEinstein.jpg)

[Robert A. Millikan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Andrews_Millikan "Robert Andrews Millikan"), [Georges Lemaître](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georges_Lema%C3%AEtre "Georges Lemaître") and Einstein at the [California Institute of Technology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_Institute_of_Technology "California Institute of Technology") in January 1933

In 1917, Einstein applied the general theory of relativity to the structure of the universe as a whole.[[251]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-257) He discovered that the general field equations predicted a universe that was dynamic, either contracting or expanding. As observational evidence for a dynamic universe was lacking at the time, Einstein introduced a new term, the [cosmological constant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cosmological_constant "Cosmological constant"), into the field equations, in order to allow the theory to predict a static universe. The modified field equations predicted a static universe of closed curvature, in accordance with Einstein's understanding of [Mach's principle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mach%27s_principle "Mach's principle") in these years. This model became known as the Einstein World or [Einstein's static universe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Einstein%27s_static_universe "Einstein's static universe").[[252]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPais1994285%E2%80%93286-258)[[253]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-iJwuX-259)

Following the discovery of the recession of the galaxies by [Edwin Hubble](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edwin_Hubble "Edwin Hubble") in 1929, Einstein abandoned his static model of the universe, and proposed two dynamic models of the cosmos, the [Friedmann–Einstein universe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Friedmann%E2%80%93Einstein_universe "Friedmann–Einstein universe") of 1931[[254]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-E1931-260)[[255]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-cor-2013-261) and the [Einstein–de Sitter universe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Einstein%E2%80%93de_Sitter_universe "Einstein–de Sitter universe") of 1932.[[256]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-262)[[257]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-J9Tqu-263) In each of these models, Einstein discarded the cosmological constant, claiming that it was "in any case theoretically unsatisfactory".[[254]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-E1931-260)[[255]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-cor-2013-261)[[258]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-sxfvo-264)

In many Einstein biographies, it is claimed that Einstein referred to the cosmological constant in later years as his "biggest blunder", based on a letter [George Gamow](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Gamow "George Gamow") claimed to have received from him. The astrophysicist [Mario Livio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mario_Livio "Mario Livio") has cast doubt on this claim.[[259]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-qmmVf-265)

In late 2013, a team led by the Irish physicist [Cormac O'Raifeartaigh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cormac_O%27Raifeartaigh "Cormac O'Raifeartaigh") discovered evidence that, shortly after learning of Hubble's observations of the recession of the galaxies, Einstein considered a [steady-state model](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steady-state_model "Steady-state model") of the universe.[[260]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Tq53z-266)[[261]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-8pfEk-267) In a hitherto overlooked manuscript, apparently written in early 1931, Einstein explored a model of the expanding universe in which the density of matter remains constant due to a continuous creation of matter, a process that he associated with the cosmological constant.[[262]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-cor-steady-state-268)[[263]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Einstein's_aborted_model-269) As he stated in the paper, In what follows, I would like to draw attention to a solution to equation (1) that can account for Hubbel's [_[sic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sic "Sic")_] facts, and in which the density is constant over time [...] If one considers a physically bounded volume, particles of matter will be continually leaving it. For the density to remain constant, new particles of matter must be continually formed in the volume from space.

It thus appears that Einstein considered a [steady-state model](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steady-state_model "Steady-state model") of the expanding universe many years before Hoyle, Bondi and Gold.[[264]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-ILjYQ-270)[[265]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-ThZb0-271) However, Einstein's steady-state model contained a fundamental flaw and he quickly abandoned the idea.[[262]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-cor-steady-state-268)[[263]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Einstein's_aborted_model-269)[[266]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-7ShC9-272)

#### Energy momentum pseudotensor

General relativity includes a dynamical spacetime, so it is difficult to see how to identify the conserved energy and momentum. [Noether's theorem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Noether%27s_theorem "Noether's theorem") allows these quantities to be determined from a [Lagrangian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lagrangian_(field_theory) "Lagrangian (field theory)") with [translation invariance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Translation_invariance "Translation invariance"), but [general covariance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_covariance "General covariance") makes translation invariance into something of a [gauge symmetry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gauge_symmetry "Gauge symmetry"). The energy and momentum derived within general relativity by [Noether](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emmy_Noether "Emmy Noether")'s prescriptions do not make a real tensor for this reason.[[267]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-273)

Einstein argued that this is true for a fundamental reason: the gravitational field could be made to vanish by a choice of coordinates. He maintained that the non-covariant energy momentum pseudotensor was, in fact, the best description of the energy momentum distribution in a gravitational field. While the use of non-covariant objects like pseudotensors was criticized by [Erwin Schrödinger](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Erwin_Schr%C3%B6dinger "Erwin Schrödinger") and others, Einstein's approach has been echoed by physicists including [Lev Landau](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lev_Landau "Lev Landau") and [Evgeny Lifshitz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evgeny_Lifshitz "Evgeny Lifshitz").[[268]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-274)

#### Wormholes

In 1935, Einstein collaborated with [Nathan Rosen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nathan_Rosen "Nathan Rosen") to produce a model of a [wormhole](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wormhole "Wormhole"), often called [Einstein–Rosen bridges](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Einstein%E2%80%93Rosen_bridges "Einstein–Rosen bridges").[[269]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-275)[[270]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-QNjpt-276) His motivation was to model elementary particles with charge as a solution of gravitational field equations, in line with the program outlined in the paper "Do Gravitational Fields play an Important Role in the Constitution of the Elementary Particles?". These solutions cut and pasted [Schwarzschild black holes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Schwarzschild_black_hole "Schwarzschild black hole") to make a bridge between two patches. Because these solutions included spacetime curvature without the presence of a physical body, Einstein and Rosen suggested that they could provide the beginnings of a theory that avoided the notion of point particles. However, it was later found that Einstein–Rosen bridges are not stable.[[271]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-ja7FY-277)

#### Einstein–Cartan theory

[![Image 30: Einstein, sitting at a table, looks up from the papers he is reading and into the camera.](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Albert_Einstein_photo_1920.jpg/250px-Albert_Einstein_photo_1920.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Albert_Einstein_photo_1920.jpg)

Einstein at his office, [University of Berlin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Berlin "University of Berlin"), 1920

In order to incorporate spinning point particles into general relativity, the affine connection needed to be generalized to include an antisymmetric part, called the [torsion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Torsion_tensor "Torsion tensor"). This modification was made by Einstein and Cartan in the 1920s.

#### Equations of motion

In general relativity, gravitational force is reimagined as curvature of [spacetime](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spacetime "Spacetime"). A curved path like an orbit is not the result of a force deflecting a body from an ideal straight-line path, but rather the body's attempt to fall freely through a background that is itself curved by the presence of other masses. A remark by [John Archibald Wheeler](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Archibald_Wheeler "John Archibald Wheeler") that has become proverbial among physicists summarizes the theory: Spacetime tells matter how to move; matter tells spacetime how to curve.[[272]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Wheeler-278)[[273]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-279) The [Einstein field equations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Einstein_field_equations "Einstein field equations") cover the latter aspect of the theory, relating the curvature of spacetime to the distribution of matter and energy. The [geodesic equation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geodesic_equation "Geodesic equation") covers the former aspect, stating that freely falling bodies follow [lines that are as straight as possible in a curved spacetime](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geodesics_in_general_relativity "Geodesics in general relativity"). Einstein regarded this as an "independent fundamental assumption" that had to be postulated in addition to the field equations in order to complete the theory. Believing this to be a shortcoming in how general relativity was originally presented, he wished to derive it from the field equations themselves. Since the equations of general relativity are non-linear, a lump of energy made out of pure gravitational fields, like a black hole, would move on a trajectory which is determined by the Einstein field equations themselves, not by a new law. Accordingly, Einstein proposed that the field equations would determine the path of a singular solution, like a black hole, to be a geodesic. Both physicists and philosophers have often repeated the assertion that the geodesic equation can be obtained from applying the field equations to the motion of a [gravitational singularity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gravitational_singularity "Gravitational singularity"), but this claim remains disputed.[[274]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-280)[[275]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-281)

### Old quantum theory

#### Photons and energy quanta

[![Image 31](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Photoelectric_effect_in_a_solid_-_diagram.svg/250px-Photoelectric_effect_in_a_solid_-_diagram.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Photoelectric_effect_in_a_solid_-_diagram.svg)

The photoelectric effect. Incoming photons on the left strike a metal plate (bottom), and eject electrons, depicted as flying off to the right.

In a 1905 paper,[[223]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-1905a-227) Einstein postulated that light itself consists of localized particles (_[quanta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum "Quantum")_). Einstein's light quanta were nearly universally rejected by all physicists, including Max Planck and Niels Bohr. This idea only became universally accepted in 1919, with [Robert Millikan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Millikan "Robert Millikan")'s detailed experiments on the photoelectric effect, and with the measurement of [Compton scattering](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Compton_scattering "Compton scattering").

Einstein concluded that each wave of frequency _f_ is associated with a collection of photons with energy _hf_ each, where _h_ is the [Planck constant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planck_constant "Planck constant"). He did not say much more, because he was not sure how the particles were related to the wave. But he did suggest that this idea would explain certain experimental results, notably the [photoelectric effect](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Photoelectric_effect "Photoelectric effect").[[223]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-1905a-227) Light quanta were dubbed _[photons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Photons "Photons")_ by [Gilbert N. Lewis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gilbert_N._Lewis "Gilbert N. Lewis") in 1926.[[276]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007576-282)

#### Quantized atomic vibrations

In 1907, Einstein proposed a model of matter where each atom in a lattice structure is an independent harmonic oscillator. In the Einstein model, each atom oscillates independently—a series of equally spaced quantized states for each oscillator. Einstein was aware that getting the frequency of the actual oscillations would be difficult, but he nevertheless proposed this theory because it was a particularly clear demonstration that quantum mechanics could solve the specific heat problem in classical mechanics. [Peter Debye](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_Debye "Peter Debye") refined this model.[[277]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-ixm32-283)

#### Bose–Einstein statistics

In 1924, Einstein received a description of a [statistical](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistical_mechanics "Statistical mechanics") model from Indian physicist [Satyendra Nath Bose](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Satyendra_Nath_Bose "Satyendra Nath Bose"), based on a counting method that assumed that light could be understood as a gas of indistinguishable particles. Einstein noted that Bose's statistics applied to some atoms as well as to the proposed light particles, and submitted his translation of Bose's paper to the _[Zeitschrift für Physik](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zeitschrift\_f%C3%BCr\_Physik "Zeitschrift für Physik")_. Einstein also published his own articles describing the model and its implications, among them the [Bose–Einstein condensate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bose%E2%80%93Einstein_condensate "Bose–Einstein condensate") phenomenon that some particulates should appear at very low temperatures.[[278]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-284) It was not until 1995 that the first such condensate was produced experimentally by [Eric Allin Cornell](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eric_Allin_Cornell "Eric Allin Cornell") and [Carl Wieman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carl_Wieman "Carl Wieman") using [ultra-cooling](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ultracold_atom "Ultracold atom") equipment built at the [NIST](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NIST "NIST")–[JILA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/JILA "JILA") laboratory at the [University of Colorado at Boulder](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Colorado_at_Boulder "University of Colorado at Boulder").[[279]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-nlagl-285) Bose–Einstein statistics are now used to describe the behaviors of any assembly of [bosons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boson "Boson"). Einstein's sketches for this project may be seen in the Einstein Archive in the library of the Leiden University.[[219]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Instituut-Lorentz-223)

#### Wave–particle duality

[![Image 32](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Albert_Einstein_1921_%28re-cropped%29.jpg/250px-Albert_Einstein_1921_%28re-cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Albert_Einstein_1921_(re-cropped).jpg)

Einstein in 1921, by [Harris & Ewing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harris_%26_Ewing "Harris & Ewing") studio

Although the patent office promoted Einstein to Technical Examiner Second Class in 1906, he had not given up on academia. In 1908, he became a _[Privatdozent](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Privatdozent "Privatdozent")_ at the University of Bern.[[280]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPais1982522-286) In "_Über die Entwicklung unserer Anschauungen über das Wesen und die Konstitution der Strahlung_" ("[The Development of our Views on the Composition and Essence of Radiation](https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Translation:The_Development_of_Our_Views_on_the_Composition_and_Essence_of_Radiation "s:Translation:The Development of Our Views on the Composition and Essence of Radiation")"), on the [quantization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantization_(physics) "Quantization (physics)") of light, and in an earlier 1909 paper, Einstein showed that Max Planck's energy quanta must have well-defined [momenta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Momentum "Momentum") and act in some respects as independent, [point-like particles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Point_particle "Point particle"). This paper introduced the _photon_ concept and inspired the notion of [wave–particle duality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wave%E2%80%93particle_duality "Wave–particle duality") in quantum mechanics. Einstein saw this wave–particle duality in radiation as concrete evidence for his conviction that physics needed a new, unified foundation.

#### Zero-point energy

In a series of works completed from 1911 to 1913, Planck reformulated his 1900 quantum theory and introduced the idea of [zero-point energy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zero-point_energy "Zero-point energy") in his "second quantum theory". Soon, this idea attracted the attention of Einstein and his assistant [Otto Stern](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Otto_Stern "Otto Stern"). Assuming the energy of rotating diatomic molecules contains zero-point energy, they then compared the theoretical specific heat of hydrogen gas with the experimental data. The numbers matched nicely. However, after publishing the findings, they promptly withdrew their support, because they no longer had confidence in the correctness of the idea of zero-point energy.[[281]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-287)

#### Stimulated emission

In 1917, at the height of his work on relativity, Einstein published an article in _Physikalische Zeitschrift_ that proposed the possibility of [stimulated emission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stimulated_emission "Stimulated emission"), the physical process that makes possible the [maser](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maser "Maser") and the [laser](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Laser "Laser").[[282]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-288) This article showed that the statistics of absorption and emission of light would only be consistent with Planck's distribution law if the emission of light into a mode with n photons would be enhanced statistically compared to the emission of light into an empty mode. This paper was enormously influential in the later development of quantum mechanics, because it was the first paper to show that the statistics of atomic transitions had simple laws.[[283]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-289)

#### Matter waves

Einstein discovered [Louis de Broglie](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_de_Broglie "Louis de Broglie")'s work and supported his ideas, which were received skeptically at first. In another major paper from this era, Einstein observed that [de Broglie waves](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/De_Broglie_waves "De Broglie waves") could explain the [quantization rules of Bohr and Sommerfeld](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bohr-Sommerfeld_quantization "Bohr-Sommerfeld quantization"). This paper would inspire Schrödinger's work of 1926.[[284]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-290)[[285]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-291)

### Quantum mechanics

#### Einstein's objections to quantum mechanics

[![Image 33](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/NYT_May_4%2C_1935.jpg/250px-NYT_May_4%2C_1935.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:NYT_May_4,_1935.jpg)

Newspaper headline on 4 May 1935

Einstein played a major role in developing quantum theory, beginning with his 1905 paper on the photoelectric effect. However, he became displeased with modern quantum mechanics as it had evolved after 1925, despite its acceptance by other physicists. He was skeptical that the randomness of quantum mechanics was fundamental rather than the result of determinism, stating that God "is not playing at dice".[[286]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-zZ2hS-292) Until the end of his life, he continued to maintain that quantum mechanics was incomplete.[[287]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-yzZtL-293)

#### Bohr versus Einstein

[![Image 34: Two men sitting, looking relaxed. A dark-haired Bohr is talking while Einstein looks skeptical.](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Niels_Bohr_Albert_Einstein4_by_Ehrenfest_cr.jpg/250px-Niels_Bohr_Albert_Einstein4_by_Ehrenfest_cr.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Niels_Bohr_Albert_Einstein4_by_Ehrenfest_cr.jpg)

Einstein and [Niels Bohr](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Niels_Bohr "Niels Bohr"), 1925

The Bohr–Einstein debates were a series of public disputes about quantum mechanics between Einstein and [Niels Bohr](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Niels_Bohr "Niels Bohr"), who were two of its founders. Their debates are remembered because of their importance to the [philosophy of science](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philosophy_of_science "Philosophy of science").[[288]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Bohr1949-294)[[289]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-295)[[290]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-296) Their debates would influence later [interpretations of quantum mechanics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interpretations_of_quantum_mechanics "Interpretations of quantum mechanics").

#### Einstein–Podolsky–Rosen paradox

Einstein never fully accepted quantum mechanics. While he recognized that it made correct predictions, he believed a more fundamental description of nature must be possible. Over the years he presented multiple arguments to this effect, but the one he preferred most dated to a debate with Bohr in 1930. Einstein suggested a [thought experiment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Einstein%27s_thought_experiments "Einstein's thought experiments") in which two objects are allowed to interact and then moved apart a great distance from each other. The quantum-mechanical description of the two objects is a mathematical entity known as a [wavefunction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wavefunction "Wavefunction"). If the wavefunction that describes the two objects before their interaction is given, then the [Schrödinger equation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Schr%C3%B6dinger_equation "Schrödinger equation") provides the wavefunction that describes them after their interaction. But because of what would later be called [quantum entanglement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_entanglement "Quantum entanglement"), measuring one object would lead to an instantaneous change of the wavefunction describing the other object, no matter how far away it is. Moreover, the choice of which measurement to perform upon the first object would affect what wavefunction could result for the second object. Einstein reasoned that no influence could propagate from the first object to the second instantaneously fast. Indeed, he argued, physics depends on being able to tell one thing apart from another, and such instantaneous influences would call that into question. Because the true "physical condition" of the second object could not be immediately altered by an action done to the first, Einstein concluded, the wavefunction could not be that true physical condition, only an incomplete description of it.[[291]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoward1990-297)[[292]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarriganSpekkens2010-298)

A more famous version of this argument came in 1935, when Einstein published a paper with [Boris Podolsky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boris_Podolsky "Boris Podolsky") and [Nathan Rosen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nathan_Rosen "Nathan Rosen") that laid out what would become known as the [EPR paradox](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/EPR_paradox "EPR paradox").[[293]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-299) In this thought experiment, two particles interact in such a way that the wavefunction describing them is entangled. Then, no matter how far the two particles were separated, a precise position measurement on one particle would imply the ability to predict, perfectly, the result of measuring the position of the other particle. Likewise, a precise momentum measurement of one particle would result in an equally precise prediction for of the momentum of the other particle, without needing to disturb the other particle in any way. They argued that no action taken on the first particle could instantaneously affect the other, since this would involve information being transmitted faster than light, which is forbidden by the [theory of relativity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theory_of_relativity "Theory of relativity"). They invoked a principle, later known as the "EPR criterion of reality", positing that: If, without in any way disturbing a system, we can predict with certainty (i.e., with [probability](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Probability "Probability") equal to unity) the value of a physical quantity, then there exists an element of reality corresponding to that quantity. From this, they inferred that the second particle must have a definite value of both position and of momentum prior to either quantity being measured. But quantum mechanics considers these two observables [incompatible](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Observable#Incompatibility_of_observables_in_quantum_mechanics "Observable") and thus does not associate simultaneous values for both to any system. Einstein, Podolsky, and Rosen therefore concluded that quantum theory does not provide a complete description of reality.[[294]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeres2002-300)

In 1964, [John Stewart Bell](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Stewart_Bell "John Stewart Bell") carried the analysis of quantum entanglement much further. He deduced that if measurements are performed independently on the two separated particles of an entangled pair, then the assumption that the outcomes depend upon hidden variables within each half implies a mathematical constraint on how the outcomes on the two measurements are correlated. This constraint would later be called a [Bell inequality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bell_inequality "Bell inequality"). Bell then showed that quantum physics predicts correlations that violate this inequality. Consequently, the only way that hidden variables could explain the predictions of quantum physics is if they are "nonlocal", which is to say that somehow the two particles are able to interact instantaneously no matter how widely they ever become separated.[[295]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMermin1993-301)[[296]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPenrose2007-302) Bell argued that because an explanation of quantum phenomena in terms of hidden variables would require nonlocality, the EPR paradox is resolved in the way which Einstein would have liked least.[[297]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBell1966-303)

Despite this, and although Einstein personally found the argument in the EPR paper overly complicated,[[291]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoward1990-297)[[292]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarriganSpekkens2010-298) that paper became among the most influential papers published in _[Physical Review](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Physical\_Review "Physical Review")_. It is considered a centerpiece of the development of [quantum information theory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_information_theory "Quantum information theory").[[298]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFine2017-304)

### Unified field theory

Encouraged by his success with general relativity, Einstein sought an even more ambitious geometrical theory that would treat gravitation and electromagnetism as aspects of a single entity. In 1950, he described his [unified field theory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unified_field_theory "Unified field theory") in a _[Scientific American](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scientific\_American "Scientific American")_ article titled "On the Generalized Theory of Gravitation".[[299]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-305) His attempt to find the most fundamental laws of nature won him praise but not success: a particularly conspicuous blemish of his model was that it did not accommodate the [strong](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Strong_nuclear_force "Strong nuclear force") and [weak nuclear forces](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Weak_nuclear_force "Weak nuclear force"), neither of which was well understood until many years after his death. Although most researchers now believe that Einstein's approach to unifying physics was mistaken, his goal of a [theory of everything](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theory_of_everything "Theory of everything") is one to which his successors still aspire.[[300]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-306)

### Other investigations

Einstein conducted other investigations that were unsuccessful and abandoned. These pertain to [force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Force "Force"), [superconductivity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Superconductivity "Superconductivity"), and other research.

### Collaboration with other scientists

[![Image 35](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Solvay_conference_1927.jpg/250px-Solvay_conference_1927.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Solvay_conference_1927.jpg)

The 1927 [Solvay Conference](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solvay_Conference "Solvay Conference") in Brussels, a gathering of the world's top physicists. Einstein is in the center.

In addition to longtime collaborators [Leopold Infeld](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leopold_Infeld "Leopold Infeld"), [Nathan Rosen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nathan_Rosen "Nathan Rosen"), [Peter Bergmann](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_Bergmann "Peter Bergmann") and others, Einstein also had some one-shot collaborations with various scientists.

#### Einstein–de Haas experiment

In 1908, [Owen Willans Richardson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Owen_Willans_Richardson "Owen Willans Richardson") predicted that a change in the [magnetic moment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magnetic_moment "Magnetic moment") of a free body will cause this body to rotate.
