This effect is a consequence of the [conservation of angular momentum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conservation_of_angular_momentum "Conservation of angular momentum") and is strong enough to be observable in [ferromagnetic materials](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ferromagnetic_materials "Ferromagnetic materials").[[301]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Richardson-1908-307) Einstein and [Wander Johannes de Haas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wander_Johannes_de_Haas "Wander Johannes de Haas") published two papers in 1915 claiming the first experimental observation of the effect.[[302]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-EdH-1-1915-308)[[303]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-EdH-2-1915-309) Measurements of this kind demonstrate that the phenomenon of [magnetization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magnetization "Magnetization") is caused by the alignment ([polarization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spin_polarization "Spin polarization")) of the [angular momenta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Angular_momenta "Angular momenta") of the [electrons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electron "Electron") in the material along the axis of magnetization. These measurements also allow the separation of the two contributions to the magnetization: that which is associated with the [spin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spin_(physics) "Spin (physics)") and with the orbital motion of the electrons. The Einstein-de Haas experiment is the only experiment conceived, realized and published by Albert Einstein himself.

A complete original version of the Einstein-de Haas experimental equipment was donated by [Geertruida de Haas-Lorentz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geertruida_de_Haas-Lorentz "Geertruida de Haas-Lorentz"), wife of de Haas and daughter of Lorentz, to the [Ampère Museum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amp%C3%A8re_Museum "Ampère Museum") in Lyon France in 1961 where it is currently on display. It was lost among the museum's holdings and was rediscovered in 2023.[[304]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-310)[[305]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-311)

#### Einstein as an inventor

In 1926, Einstein and his former student [Leó Szilárd](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Le%C3%B3_Szil%C3%A1rd "Leó Szilárd") co-invented (and in 1930, patented) the [Einstein refrigerator](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Einstein_refrigerator "Einstein refrigerator"). This [absorption refrigerator](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Absorption_refrigerator "Absorption refrigerator") was then revolutionary for having no moving parts and using only heat as an input.[[306]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Goettling-312) On 11 November 1930, [U.S. patent 1,781,541](https://patents.google.com/patent/US1781541) was awarded to Einstein and Leó Szilárd for the refrigerator. Their invention was not immediately put into commercial production, but the most promising of their patents were acquired by the Swedish company [Electrolux](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electrolux "Electrolux").[[note 6]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-314)

Einstein also invented an electromagnetic pump,[[308]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-patents.google.com-315) sound reproduction device,[[309]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-316) and several other household devices.[[310]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-317)

Legacy
------

### Non-scientific

[![Image 36](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Einstein-Oslofjord_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Einstein-Oslofjord_%28cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Einstein-Oslofjord_(cropped).jpg)

Left-right: [Heinrich Goldschmidt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heinrich_Jacob_Goldschmidt "Heinrich Jacob Goldschmidt"), Einstein, [Ole Colbjørnsen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ole_Colbj%C3%B8rnsen "Ole Colbjørnsen"), [Jørgen Vogt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/J%C3%B8rgen_Vogt "Jørgen Vogt"), and Ilse Einstein at a picnic in Oslo in 1920.

While traveling, Einstein wrote daily to his wife Elsa and adopted stepdaughters Margot and Ilse. The letters were included in the papers bequeathed to the [Hebrew University of Jerusalem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hebrew_University_of_Jerusalem "Hebrew University of Jerusalem"). Margot Einstein permitted the personal letters to be made available to the public, but requested that it not be done until twenty years after her death (she died in 1986[[311]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-margot-obituary-318)). Barbara Wolff, of the Hebrew University's [Albert Einstein Archives](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein_Archives "Albert Einstein Archives"), told the [BBC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BBC "BBC") that there are about 3,500 pages of private correspondence written between 1912 and 1955.[[312]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-letters-love-319)

In his final four years, Einstein was involved with the establishment of the [Albert Einstein College of Medicine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein_College_of_Medicine "Albert Einstein College of Medicine") in New York City.[[313]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-320)

In 1979, the [Albert Einstein Memorial](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein_Memorial "Albert Einstein Memorial") was unveiled outside the [National Academy of Sciences](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Academy_of_Sciences "National Academy of Sciences") building in [Washington, D.C.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Washington,_D.C. "Washington, D.C.") for the Einstein centenary. It was sculpted by [Robert Berks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Berks "Robert Berks"). Einstein can be seen holding a paper with three of his most important equations: for the [photoelectric effect](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Photoelectric_effect "Photoelectric effect"), [general relativity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_relativity "General relativity") and [mass-energy equivalence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mass-energy_equivalence "Mass-energy equivalence").[[314]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-321)

Einstein's [right of publicity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Right_of_publicity "Right of publicity") was litigated in 2015 in a federal district court in California. Although the court initially held that the right had expired,[[315]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-casetext-hebrew-university-322) that ruling was immediately appealed, and the decision was later vacated in its entirety. The underlying claims between the parties in that lawsuit were ultimately settled. The right is enforceable, and the Hebrew University of Jerusalem is the exclusive representative of that right.[[316]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-pacermonitor-hebrew-university-323)[Corbis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Branded_Entertainment_Network "Branded Entertainment Network"), successor to The Roger Richman Agency, licenses the [use of his name and associated imagery](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trademark "Trademark"), as agent for the university.[[317]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-einstein.biz-324)

[Mount Einstein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mount_Einstein "Mount Einstein") in the [Chugach Mountains](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chugach_Mountains "Chugach Mountains") of [Alaska](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alaska "Alaska") was named in 1955. Mount Einstein in New Zealand's [Paparoa Range](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paparoa_Range "Paparoa Range") was named after him in 1970 by the [Department of Scientific and Industrial Research](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Department_of_Scientific_and_Industrial_Research_(New_Zealand) "Department of Scientific and Industrial Research (New Zealand)").[[318]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-325)

In 1999, Einstein was named [_Time_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Time_(magazine) "Time (magazine)")'s [Person of the Century](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Time_100:_The_Most_Important_People_of_the_Century "Time 100: The Most Important People of the Century").[[319]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-TIME-326)

### Scientific

In 1999, a survey of the top 100 physicists voted for Einstein as the "greatest physicist ever", while a parallel survey of rank-and-file physicists gave the top spot to [Isaac Newton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isaac_Newton "Isaac Newton"), with Einstein second.[[320]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-327)[[321]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-328)

Physicist [Lev Landau](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lev_Landau "Lev Landau") ranked physicists from 0 to 5 on a [logarithmic scale](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lev_Landau#Landau's_ranking_of_physicists "Lev Landau") of productivity and genius, with Newton and Einstein belonging in a "super league", with Newton receiving the highest ranking of 0, followed by Einstein with 0.5, while fathers of quantum mechanics such as [Werner Heisenberg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Werner_Heisenberg "Werner Heisenberg") and [Paul Dirac](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Dirac "Paul Dirac") were ranked 1, with Landau himself a 2.[[322]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-329)

Physicist [Eugene Wigner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eugene_Wigner "Eugene Wigner") noted that while [John von Neumann](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann "John von Neumann") had the quickest and most acute mind he ever knew, the understanding of Einstein was deeper than von Neumann's, stating that:[[323]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-330)

> But Einstein's understanding was deeper than even Jancsi von Neumann's. His mind was both more penetrating and more original than von Neumann's. And that is a very remarkable statement. Einstein took an extraordinary pleasure in invention. Two of his greatest inventions are the Special and General Theories of Relativity; and for all of Jancsi's brilliance, he never produced anything so original. No modern physicist has.

The [International Union of Pure and Applied Physics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Union_of_Pure_and_Applied_Physics "International Union of Pure and Applied Physics") declared 2005 the "[World Year of Physics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Year_of_Physics_2005 "World Year of Physics 2005")", also known as "Einstein Year", in recognition of Einstein's "[miracle year](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Annus_mirabilis#1905_%E2%80%93_Albert_Einstein "Annus mirabilis")" in 1905.[[324]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-331) It was also declared the "International Year of Physics" by the [United Nations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations "United Nations").[[325]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-332)

In popular culture
------------------

[![Image 37](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Albert_Einstein_sticks_his_tongue.jpg/250px-Albert_Einstein_sticks_his_tongue.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Albert_Einstein_sticks_his_tongue.jpg)

The famous image of Einstein taken by [Arthur Sasse](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arthur_Sasse "Arthur Sasse") in 1951, sitting in a car on his 72nd birthday, having been asked to smile for the camera once again.

Einstein became one of the most famous [scientific celebrities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scientific_celebrity "Scientific celebrity") after the confirmation of his general theory of relativity in 1919.[[326]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-333)[[327]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-334)[[328]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-335) Although most of the public had little understanding of his work, he was widely recognized and admired. In the period before World War II, _[The New Yorker](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_New\_Yorker "The New Yorker")_ published a vignette in their "The Talk of the Town" feature saying that Einstein was so well known in America that he would be stopped on the street by people wanting him to explain "that theory". Eventually he came to cope with unwanted enquirers by pretending to be someone else: Pardon me, sorry! Always I am mistaken for Professor Einstein.[[329]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-disguise-336)

Einstein has been the subject of or inspiration for many novels, films, plays, and works of music.[[330]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-orchestra-337) He is a favorite model for depictions of [absent-minded professors](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Absent-minded_professor "Absent-minded professor"); his expressive face and distinctive hairstyle have been widely copied and exaggerated. _[Time](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Time\_(magazine) "Time (magazine)")_ magazine's Frederic Golden wrote that Einstein was "a cartoonist's dream come true".[[331]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-slqbwn-338) His intellectual achievements and originality made _Einstein_ broadly synonymous with _genius_.[[332]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-wordnetweb.princeton.edu-339)

Many popular [quotations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quotations "Quotations") are often [misattributed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/False_attribution "False attribution") to him.[[333]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-fake-quotes-340)[[334]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-humiliate-atheist-341)

Awards and honors
-----------------

Einstein received numerous awards and honors, and in 1922, he was awarded the 1921 [Nobel Prize in Physics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physics "Nobel Prize in Physics")for his services to Theoretical Physics, and especially for his discovery of the law of the photoelectric effect. None of the nominations in 1921 met the criteria set by [Alfred Nobel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alfred_Nobel "Alfred Nobel"), so the 1921 prize was carried forward and awarded to Einstein in 1922.[[7]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-Nobel_Prize-9)

[Einsteinium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Einsteinium "Einsteinium"), a synthetic chemical element, was named in his honor in 1955, a few months after his death.[[335]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-342)

Notes
-----

1.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_ref-6)**, [_EYEN-styne_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key "Help:Pronunciation respelling key");[[4]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-NDxay-5)German:[[ˈalbɛʁt ˈaɪnʃtaɪn]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA/Standard_German "Help:IPA/Standard German")[](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/7/77/De-Albert_Einstein.oga/De-Albert_Einstein.oga.mp3 "Play audio")[ⓘ](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:De-Albert_Einstein.oga "File:De-Albert Einstein.oga")

1.   ^ [_**a**_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_ref-GEcitizen_4-0)[_**b**_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_ref-GEcitizen_4-1)[_**c**_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_ref-GEcitizen_4-2)[_**d**_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_ref-GEcitizen_4-3)[_**e**_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_ref-GEcitizen_4-4)Until 1913, German citizenship was acquired through citizenship in a constituent state (whose requirements varied); from 1913, uniform citizenship requirements were [set at the national level](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_the_German_Empire#Citizenship "Constitution of the German Empire").
2.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_ref-MaturaScore_35-0)**Einstein's scores on his _[Matura](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Matura "Matura")_ certificate: German 5; French 3; Italian 5; History 6; Geography 4; Algebra 6; Geometry 6; Descriptive Geometry 6; Physics 6; Chemistry 5; Natural History 5; Art Drawing 4; Technical Drawing 4.

[Scale](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grading_systems_by_country#Switzerland "Grading systems by country"): 6 = very good, 5 = good, 4 = sufficient, 3 = insufficient, 2 = poor, 1 = very poor.
3.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_ref-gnriE_144-0)**Their leaders in Germany have not driven out her cut-throats and her blackguards. She has chosen the cream of her culture and has suppressed it. She has even turned upon her most glorious citizen, Albert Einstein, who is the supreme example of the selfless intellectual...The man, who, beyond all others, approximates a citizen of the world, is without a home. How proud we must be to offer him temporary shelter.
4.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_ref-aBfxO_236-0)**In [his paper](https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Translation:On_the_Electrodynamics_of_Moving_Bodies "s:Translation:On the Electrodynamics of Moving Bodies"), Einstein wrote: The introduction of a 'luminiferous æther' will be proved to be superfluous in so far, as according to the conceptions which will be developed, we shall introduce neither a 'space absolutely at rest' endowed with special properties, nor shall we associate a velocity-vector with a point in which electro-magnetic processes take place.
5.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_ref-sBl2q_238-0)**For a discussion of the reception of relativity theory around the world, and the different controversies it encountered, see the articles in [Glick (1987)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#CITEREFGlick1987).
6.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_ref-314)**In September 2008, it was reported that Malcolm McCulloch of [Oxford University](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxford_University "Oxford University") was heading a three-year project to develop more robust appliances that could be used in locales lacking electricity, and that his team had completed a prototype Einstein refrigerator. He was quoted as saying that improving the design and changing the types of gases used might allow the design's efficiency to be quadrupled.[[307]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein#cite_note-313)
